From the inception of the One Origin, the Two Modes were distinguished. Though the Dao Mother is the progenitor of all yin, the Empress is the mother of the ten thousand heavens. She wields the handle of life and formation, holding authority over progeny and succession. She safeguards life to protect infants, commands the expulsion of pestilence, and averts calamities—her compassion saves the suffering. Moved by the plight of sentient beings, she vows to shield the people, her boundless grace flowing through the ages.

We, fortunate to live in this flourishing era and behold the bonds of human kinship, look up in gratitude for the gift of life. May she graciously extend her hidden protection, upholding the wondrous Dao of precelestial origin to succor the people of the lower realms. Wherever utmost sincerity is offered, the power of resonance is surely attained. We now present our earnest pleas, reverently offering these fragrant supplications. Her sagely virtue is impartial, her hidden merit uncalculating. We look up in hope of her radiant witness, that she may bestow vast and enduring blessings.

We humbly pray that her phoenix chariot may pause awhile, her crane carriage tarry briefly. May past □ transgressions be pardoned, that mother and child may dwell in peace. May her grace be granted, bringing felicity to the inner chambers. Now, we—along with all officials and participants of this altar—acknowledge our karmic burdens from former kalpas to this present life: transgressions born of jealousy and harm, sins woven from wayward desire, debts recorded in the palaces of sun and moon, or bound in the celestial and terrestrial bureaus. We implore that all be absolved, that all may equally receive her benevolent protection.

May our names be inscribed in the Register of Longevity, our descendants’ names recorded for posterity. May we be granted wise and bright grandchildren from the celestial palaces. May distant ancestors and close kin alike see their descendants flourish. May inner and outer relations, roots and branches, thrive in glory. May the impurities of the mortal world not stain them, and the pestilences of the seasons not invade. Whether in water or on land, whether soaring or hidden, may all fulfill the nature of their lives.

Above, may this manifest the Empress’s virtue in safeguarding life; below, may it fulfill our devotion in taking refuge. We respectfully submit this for your celestial hearing.

**The Ten Invocations:**
First invocation: The yang of the Dao unfolds.
Second invocation: The Two Modes engender one another.
Third invocation: The Three Officials absolve sins.
Fourth invocation: The Four Courts bestow life.
Fifth invocation: The Five Phases harmonize in sequence.
Sixth invocation: The Six Palaces flourish in glory.
Seventh invocation: The Seven Stars follow their proper courses.
Eighth invocation: The Eight Directions abide in perpetual peace.
Ninth invocation: The Nine Mysteries escape suffering.
Tenth invocation: The transformation of the Dao prevails.

The incense is offered anew.

May the ministers summon the Fragrant Official Envoys, the Left and Right Dragon-Tiger Armies, the Incense-Bearing Envoys, and all attending spirit-officials of the present mandate. Here, where your servant burns incense and practices the Dao, gold fluid naturally arises, and cinnabar-green mushroom blossoms spontaneously appear. The hundred spirits and host of perfected beings gather before this incense burner. May the myriad heavens bestow their blessings, and may the entire household receive grace.

May the golden lads and jade maidens of the ten directions attend the rising incense smoke, swiftly conveying the sincerity of your servant’s earlier supplications directly to the Celestial Empress, the Primordial Sovereign of the Nine Heavens. With the ritual offerings now complete, we humbly receive her merciful grace, bowing reverently to send her off with repeated obeisance.

**Hymn of Sending Forth the Perfected:**
The ranks of the Nine Heavens stand in solemn array along the clouded avenues.
Golden lads and jade maidens bear jeweled canopies and banners.
The ladies of the celestial palaces take their places in the vanguard.
Heavenly incense fills the air with fragrance; golden lotus candles blaze.
Yellow banners and leopard-tail standards, jade scepters and dragon chariots—
Riding the clouds, they depart, returning to the Great Canopy Heaven.
Your servant gazes after them as the fragrant wind fades into stillness.
The Dao Mother bestows her mysterious teachings; the radiant blossoms return to the Grotto-Heaven.
The golden censer’s incense still curls; the jade candles’ flames yet burn.
Gazing upward, my heart remains in her presence; in longing pursuit, my will cannot advance.
May the blessings we beseech flow forth; may the ritual’s sponsor enjoy enduring years.

With the ritual offerings now complete, we pray that her merciful countenance may grant blessings and bestow grace. Together, we rely on this virtuous merit to realize the supreme Dao.

All here pay reverence.
Dedication.
Transformation of paper offerings.

**Conclusion of the Divine Maiden’s Secret Rites**

**Raising the Banner Rite of the Palace:**
The banner of the state-assisting adept stands tall, its sacred streamer soaring into the vast sky.
The myriad people gaze in devotion, turning toward the Dao; the two immortals manifest their glory, and blessings multiply in splendor.
Rain moistens the jade realm, nourishing the three paths; sunlight illumines the dragon script, penetrating the nine nights.
The chanting resounds beneath the golden turtle’s twin towers, where embodied beings receive deliverance and boundless joy.

We humbly submit: the Dao aligns with the heart, and the immortal rites are fully prepared for the covenant with the Perfected. The banner, lifted by the wind, serves as a numinous model to augment blessings and grace. As we, still bound by worldly dust, pray for peace in the turning seasons, may the lunar essence and solar spirit not obscure the moments of breath. In heaven’s halls and earth’s prisons, let awakening and reflection prevail. Recognize the wisdom of those who came before, like the tortoise and oracle; let your resolve grow firmer than the pine and cypress.

A thousand jun of precious jade cannot buy back youth; the long rope of ten thousand kalpas cannot restrain the fleeting sun. Filth and desire press like boiling snow; knowing repentance, sins may yet be dissolved. The world is but emptiness, yet the Yellow Springs record all. Moved by compassion for the departed and grief for the lost, we invoke the present to reach the hidden souls. Shedding past karma and severing illusory ties, we plant the seeds of numinous blessings to extend grace.

How dare we expect blessings unearned? How can fortune be sought for oneself alone? When people cultivate good fruits, heaven’s blessings surely follow. A boat adrift at midnight strays amid ten thousand ravines; a flower plucked before spring bears fruit at the head of all blossoms. With wholehearted devotion and diligent practice, one awakens to the Dao’s freedom. Those who seek permanence shall attain long life. Thus, we perform this rite to dispel calamity and distress, that one may pass through suffering unscathed and the body be suffused with light.

The assembly, in reverent sincerity, raises the sacred name:

**Heavenly Worthy of the Numinous Banner Who Absolves Sins**
The banner soars aloft; misfortunes and calamities vanish.
Heaven’s mercy opens the amnesty, boundless across the ten directions.
The living and the dead receive grace, all benefiting without limit.
Goodness is rewarded; cultivation is never forgotten.
Swiftly realize true emptiness, escaping impermanence.
A century of peace and well-being, guiding the reins to heaven’s halls.

*Response:* May we attain long life.

The banners rise high, following the freedom of flight.
Deep sins are wholly erased; past foolishness is awakened.
If sins dwell at the banner’s base, they may be dissolved.
If sins are ground away before the banner, they may be absolved.
Though stained as one condemned by law, one may yet awaken with a willing heart.
Strive for self-realization.
With a luminous mind, one gains blessings in abundance.
Bearing auspicious gatherings to unfold splendor, bestowing long years in celebration.
May we flourish in sublime fortune, ever praying for compassion.

The assembly, in reverent sincerity, raises the sacred name:

**Heavenly Worthy of the Jeweled Banner Who Extends Blessings**
The banner’s measure, long or short, accords with its symbol.
Blessings follow the banner; sins are ground away toward fortune.
Its mysteries are revealed, sweeping away karmic obstacles.
Long life and added years, delivering countless beings.

*Response:* May we attain long life.

Sins may indeed be absolved; blessings may be extended.
Yet if sins accumulate unceasingly, how can one claim all misdeeds are ended?
If blessings are extended without reflection, how dare one rest complacent?
To act recklessly and err is to deeply betray the meaning of reverent cultivation.
Bound souls suffer blows, ever caught between past and future lapses.
Departed spirits sink in darkness, their beginnings and ends unguarded.
Reflect on past mistakes; let no fault mar the numinous banner.
Do not idly let a hundred years of white hair pass, drifting through life.
Who says a single verse of gold surpasses all? It is but expedient teaching.
Thus, we grasp the root and lift the tail, holding fast from beginning to end.
To preserve goodness for the future, we rely further on the merciful honored ones.

The assembly, in reverent sincerity, raises the sacred name:

**Heavenly Worthy of Deliverance and Contemplating Emptiness**
Through kalpas without end, the illusory mechanisms persist.
Heaven opens the source, washing clean the body.
Disasters forever cease; blessings and prosperity converge.
Enduring years, undying, merging with the Dao in truth.

*Response:* May we attain long life.

We humbly pray that, having planted the seeds of merit, the imperial realm may stand firm, and the emperor’s Dao flourish afar. May the myriad people rejoice in peace, and the four barbarians submit to transformation. May all beings receive grace, blessings spread abundantly, sins dissolve, and good fortune gather. May the living gain blessings, and the hidden realms receive grace.

For these causes, we invoke:
The Heavenly Worthies of the Three Clarities and Three Realms,
The Heavenly Worthy Who Bestows Blessings from the Nine Heavens,
The Heavenly Worthies of the Numinous Treasure of the Ten Directions,
and their inconceivable merits.

**Conclusion of the Banner-Raising Rite of the Palace.**

**Divine Oracle of the Palace of Vast Grace and Numinous Aid**
**First Oracle – Supreme Auspice**
The dragon’s strategies and leopard’s tactics roll forth with marvelous plans.
When encountering enlightened times, present your schemes.
The world’s ways are fraught with storms and fierce currents;
better to dwell in stillness, carefully weighing rise and fall.

**Second Oracle – Supreme Supreme Auspice**
Auspicious dreams foretell good fortune first;
delve deep to find what truly pleases the heart.
Though a son may not fulfill the bow’s ambition,
high office shall yet come with another jade scepter.

**Third Oracle – Medium Auspice**
When the Green Emperor reigns at the appointed hour,
crimson and pale green adorn the flowering branches.
If the Western Wind rises one night in Shanglin Park,
does the traveler in the heavens know or not?

**Fourth Oracle – Inauspicious**
Tribal strife wounds all, and all is vain—
his benevolence, my righteousness, yet we return to the start.
Like Zou Yang imprisoned, the message sinks into silence;
who will present the plea of Lady Tiying?

**Fifth Oracle – Great Auspice**
When asking of the road ahead, rein in your haste;
better to cross the calm river with boat and oar.
Tonight the bright moon reaches its fullest,
and the cloud-lit thoroughfare stretches ten thousand miles.

**Sixth Oracle – Great Auspice**
A single current surges eastward,
while people stand gazing at the vastness.
At Western Mountain, dogs bark beneath wind and moon—
from here, the path to the azure clouds lies open.

**Seventh Oracle – Inauspicious**
A frail, ailing body defies all medicine;
hold back the finest remedies and prescriptions.
When Rabbit meets Ram, fortune will come at last—
lest joy turn to sorrow, take care.

**Eighth Oracle – Medium-Lower Auspice**
Losing an ox or a horse brings no cause for grief;
why fret over worldly affairs and seek needless trouble?
If it be early spring or late winter,
let the fair one not seek counsel by the roadside.

**Ninth Oracle – Inauspicious**
Thin clouds and lingering mist block the gate;
east, west, south, north—none flow freely.
Cast your lot where life takes you;
as autumn’s leaf falls, the crow flies past the wild goose.

**Tenth Oracle**
Though rumors fill the hall, pay them no heed—
even false words should not be trusted.
A man’s marriage will end in good fortune;
hesitation unresolved may yet see matters resolved.

**Eleventh Oracle**
Broken seals reveal vermilion edicts in rows;
ten thousand miles of azure clouds rise in joy.
The osprey soars across the sky—good tidings come—
do not linger in the mountains or beneath the trees.

**Twelfth Oracle**
In the cold valley, yang returns, surpassing nature’s craft;
idle blossoms need not blame the spring wind.
Though news from afar may seem desolate,
the cardamom branch bears its fragrance with intent.

**Thirteenth Oracle**
When perch grows fat and autumn thoughts arise,
a thousand acres of waves await the hook.
The gull reveals the mechanism, flying in vain—
how can one bear the full moon filling the returning boat?

**Fourteenth Oracle**
With strength on my side and weakness on theirs, I plant the banner of surrender;
do not speak of injustice to the traveler.
Though rain clears and clouds disperse, the storm is not yet stilled—
only when the spring wind arrives will all become clear.

**Fifteenth Oracle**
Why measure and weigh again and again?
Wings poised for flight aim southward.
Yet suddenly, messages bring obstruction—
if the matter succeeds, it may yet prove unbearable.

**Sixteenth Oracle – Inauspicious**
A lone soldier wanders at the edge of the sky;
the tiger lurks in the *yin* direction, while home is longed for.
Day by day, the spirit fades, and word is lost—
a branch of pear blossoms, rain-laden, slants.

**Seventeenth Oracle – Medium-Lower Auspice**
When the Vermilion Bird governs the *bing* direction,
do not dwell on the misfortune of descendants.
Where the wind and waves are calm, step forward;
beware the sting of wasps and the harm of ginger—do not wound yourself.

**Eighteenth Oracle – Medium Auspice**
A noble guest at Dragon Gate brings fresh joy;
in the celestial thoroughfare, wings cling to scales.
Casually ask of the path of patronage—
the Rabbit’s modest talent sighs over broken kindling.

**Nineteenth Oracle – Official Matters**
Ten thousand changes on the branch refuse to cease;
sworn brothers and sworn mothers weave enmity.
Best to swiftly resolve past transgressions—
seek the gods’ favor through rites to dispel sorrow.

**Twentieth Oracle – Auspicious**
Peach and plum in the vermilion gate are adorned;
the work of rain and dew shines in radiant sunlight.
At the first strum of wind and cloud, the moment arrives—
do not speak of returning home in brocade too soon.

**Twenty-First Oracle – Medium Auspice**
Why crave wealth and profit so greedily?
Do not trust sweet words that are not yet fully pleasing.
All prosperous merchants reap interest—
joyful hues abound in the southeast.

**Twenty-Second Oracle – Auspicious**
Carriages and travelers come and go as they please;
idle flowers and cold buds press urgently.
Unaided by even a breath of wind’s force,
they steal half the night to bloom over the wall.

**Twenty-Third Oracle – Inauspicious**
It is not that a single heart is hard to find—
do not chase after works that fill ox-carts.
For in the end, causes and conditions will become clear;
who in the groves and springs will recognize true appreciation?

**Twenty-Fourth Oracle – Medium Auspice**
Lofty horns stand out among the chickens,
yet the clover’s fragrance refuses to part.
When the osmanthus seed carries its scent, word will come—
one morning, your name will be heard at the emperor’s side.

**Twenty-Fifth Oracle – Inauspicious**
Above, they feed on withered soil; below, the Yellow Springs;
a pair of wild geese fly high, sleeping in two places.
Two rivers flow, yet no one is seen—
the perils of worldly affairs surpass even mountains and streams.

**Twenty-Sixth Oracle – Medium Auspice**
Hearts in harmony, intentions aligned, the two unite;
the jade candle shines bright, offering many blessings.
Yet rejoice that the household knows no thieves’ path—
what of the lone star at the door this evening?

**Twenty-Seventh Oracle – Inauspicious**
Fate is harsh, the body in decline—autumn arrives;
ghosts and spirits conspire in darkness.
Beneath wind and moon, amidst flowers and wine,
lest joy turn to sorrow, take heed.

**Twenty-Eighth Oracle – Medium-Lower Auspice**
A limited view can never grasp the workings of the Dao;
nature’s craft is too subtle to emulate.
All worldly affairs are but a game of chess—
dragons and snakes in the east rise and fly as they will.

**Twenty-Ninth Oracle – Upper-Medium Auspice**
The dried fish bows its tail toward the clear stream;
a faint thread of life lingers, nearly spent.
Wait for the third surge of Yu’s Gate—
the bright pearl will not be cast into darkness.

**Thirtieth Oracle – Upper Auspice**
Weary of the world’s shifting cold and heat,
drawing snakes and severing cranes, one loses innocence.
Yet let no delay linger at the gate—
beneath the brush, spring returns, surpassing nature’s art.

**Thirty-First Oracle – Upper Auspice**
Why ask of right and wrong in sorrow?
Observe human affairs to glimpse heaven’s design.
Where people tread the *kan* path, many find contentment—
a single lonely lamp flares anew.

**Thirty-Second Oracle – Lower Auspice**
Jade and stone on Kun Mountain remain undistinguished,
the clamor of clay pots and basins grates the ear.
When the small yields to the great, the time is not yet ripe—
abandon your hundred schemes and cease your toil.

**Thirty-Third Oracle – Lower Auspice**
Sweet and bitter you have tasted through the years,
a lifetime’s six decades passed like frost and stars.
A heart weighed down as if drunk in a worldly dream—
why rush about in vain, enslaved to empty striving?

**Thirty-Fourth Oracle – Lower Auspice**
Between heaven and earth, how many partings and meetings?
Alone you stand, poised to shore up what is frail.
Broken branches, snapped legs—these you cannot escape,
yet the fire that consumes you burns unperceived.

**Thirty-Fifth Oracle – Medium Auspice**
Suddenly from level ground a storm arises,
human affairs these years grow tangled and strange.
Like salt and plum entrusted to a master’s hand,
the five flavors blend in perfect harmony.

**Thirty-Sixth Oracle – Upper-Medium Auspice**
Barred by distance, letters and words still go astray,
spring returns to grass and trees, yet light is dim.
The sun sets on Western Mountain, leaving a fading glow—
beyond the heavens, a traveler at last draws near.

**Thirty-Seventh Oracle – Medium Auspice**
When water fills the boat, it shifts in but a moment;
returning alone, you hesitate, doubt arises.
The traveler waits with intent for the bright moon—
why seek the magic herb at the gate to meet?

**Thirty-Eighth Oracle – Lower-Medium Auspice**
Lifting your gaze, a black cloud swells on the horizon,
seeking fame at the edge of the sky, yet fame eludes.
Only when you strike the Yellow Bell will the sound ring true—
a fair wind will bear you to Penglai’s isles.

**Thirty-Ninth Oracle – Medium Auspice**
The river flows west—where is the boat you seek?
How long must you wait for merit to be complete?
Others whisper news to one another—
watch the arrow fly toward autumn’s clouds.

**Fortieth Oracle – Lower Auspice**
What of your quest for wealth and gain?
The northwest wind rises—how will you cross the river?
The pearl that fetches a price must wait awhile—
life is but a dream that drifts to Nanke.

**Forty-First Oracle – Lower Auspice**
A few branches of red and purple vie in fragrance,
petals scatter, drifting on the water’s flow.
Does the swallow nesting in the oriole’s home lack intent?
Refrain from speaking of right and wrong among men.

**Forty-Second Oracle – Medium Auspice**
Chrysanthemums wither, autumn wanes, all things decay,
old regrets and past fears return to haunt.
The black pearl emerges from the sea, its luster still concealed—
point eastward, hang up your cap, and leave it be.

**Forty-Third Oracle – Lower-Medium Auspice**
The azure bird soars into clouds, yet does not return,
trust lingers in the realm of the vague and indistinct.
The sun sets over Qin Tower, thirty thousand miles away—
beyond the white-clouded mountains lie more green peaks.

**Forty-Fourth Oracle – Medium Auspice**
Sorrow and joy lean upon each other,
all things at hand—yet you gnaw at desire’s hook.
Time is as fragile as a chicken’s wing or an egg—
soon the dead end will open to a broad thoroughfare.

**Forty-Fifth Oracle – Medium Auspice**
Renewal and reform meet with yang’s return,
the traveler at heaven’s edge gains precious wealth.
Turn your head—Lord Yi is but a hand’s span away,
do not doubt or suspect, but act without delay.

**Forty-Sixth Oracle – Medium Auspice**
The chance for fame and fortune meets three lifetimes’ fate,
a roc’s ten-thousand-mile journey lies flat in your palm.
Even the paths of ox and horse cannot compare—
where the *kan* path lies, proceed with caution.

**Forty-Seventh Oracle – Lower Auspice**
Thick clouds emerge from the mountain’s hollow, never at rest,
how many days must pass before you see green peaks again?
A gnat stings, a bee strikes—empty conflict,
yet the world clings to a hollow reputation.

**Forty-Eighth Oracle – Lower-Lower Auspice**
The ways of the world are like children’s games—beyond reason,
when affairs reach their limit, they return to their root.
Clothes lie folded in the chest—guard them well,
do not share divine communion with ghostly words.

**Forty-Ninth Oracle – Upper Auspice (Most Auspicious)**
The farmer’s fields know no year without abundance,
as times change, one turns to ask the old heavens.
The Jade Candle shines, yang is bright, the fish-leaf dream—
when autumn comes, a thousand-fold profit is gained.

**Fiftieth Oracle – Upper-Upper Auspice**
Standing by the river’s edge, you avoid the wind and waves,
heaven’s will follows man’s—what can you do?
Wait until the waters of Yu’s Gate warm in spring—
then ride the raft straight to the River of Heaven.

**Fifty-First Oracle – Lower Auspice**
Human feelings, though old, never match the new,
fifty years pass, and another decade follows.
All matters are decided in the heart—
do not debate building a house by the roadside.

**Fifty-Second Oracle – Lower-Medium Auspice**
The lone lamp’s wick is trimmed, yet sleep does not come,
tears wiped away, emotions linger close at hand.
No word arrives from ten thousand miles away—
then at dawn, the magpie’s call is suddenly heard.

**Fifty-Third Oracle – Upper Auspice (Most Auspicious)**
The times are harmonious, the year abundant, the world at peace,
from here, your hometown’s fortunes turn to prosperity.
The gods rejoice, the people cheer—good fortune is secured,
a lifetime’s heart’s desires at last find fulfillment.

**Fifty-Fourth Oracle – Lower Auspice**
Greedy for wealth, you carve stone—no jade is found,
sifting sand with care—no gold appears.
All your schemes come to naught—
beware the fire that burns the river and the heart of the door.

**Fifty-Fifth Oracle – Upper-Upper Auspice**
Long in Nanyang’s thatched hut beyond the world,
three visits rouse the dragon from its winter sleep.
All under heaven await the life-giving rain—
truly, creation’s work rivals heaven’s power.

**Fifty-Sixth Oracle – Medium Auspice**
Weary of the lakes and rivers, tired of the endless road,
your straw sandals worn thin from travel.
A hundred birds return to their nests, knowing the old way,
the moon wanes, then rounds again.

**Fifty-Seventh Oracle – Lower Auspice**
Raindrops fall like petals, snowflakes drift like blossoms,
by the river, the fisherman casts his line.
Night is still, the water cold—fish do not bite,
the boat returns empty at dawn.

**Fifty-Eighth Oracle – Medium Auspice**
The horn bow’s clear reflection gleams in the golden cup,
today’s inquiry dispels suspicion and brings joy.
A knot of doubt unravels, feelings are resolved—
from whence came the deep-seated illness?

**Fifty-Ninth Oracle – Lower Auspice**
A flawless mid-autumn moon, a full round disk,
its radiant splendor illuminates heaven and earth.
Yet for no reason, a western rain arrives—
a single bright light fades into darkness.

**Sixtieth Oracle – Lower Auspice**
How can one always meet with good fortune?
Good things are often tempered—this is the way of things.
Waiting for a rabbit or guarding a pearl—both are in vain,
wasting heart and spirit to no purpose.

**Sixty-First Oracle – Upper-Medium Auspice**

**Sixty-Second Oracle – Lower Auspice**
Gentle breezes and harmonious light belong to spring’s radiance,
the old is shed, and renewal arises like a tripod’s restoration.
For families that accumulate goodness, Heaven bestows fortune—
the courtyard brims with auspicious qi, joy overflowing.

**Sixty-Third Oracle – Medium Auspice**
The ways of the world are fickle—what can be done?
East flows the stream, west it returns, time slips away.
All affairs are predestined—ten thousand matters are foreordained,
to scheme and strive is but vain toil.

**Sixty-Fourth Oracle – Lower-Medium Auspice**
Plow the fields, dig the well, retreat to the mountain forests,
why labor the heart over a hundred affairs?
I urge the world to cease chasing profit,
for greed for fame and gain only brings mutual harm.

**Register of Miraculous Responses from the Hall of Birth – First Oracle – Upper Auspice**
Last night’s auspicious dream matched a bear’s portent,
the family’s joy fills the lane—fulfillment is near.
Confucius and the Buddha personally deliver the child,
surely a stone *qilin* from Heaven.

**Second Oracle – Medium Auspice**
Do not say a tile’s gift is unworthy of praise,
the dream clearly foretold a *hui*-serpent’s sign.
One day, bound in marriage, she will rise in nobility,
a blossom north of the *Chenxiang* Pavilion.

**Third Oracle – Lower-Medium Auspice**
Your family’s gourd vines stretch far and unbroken,
blessings flow from Heaven’s decree.
Yet fear the perils of childbirth—obstructions may arise,
best to perform good deeds to safeguard peace.

**Fourth Oracle – Lower Auspice**
In dark wind and rain, the flower droops in bloom,
scarcely opened, it is marred by blight.
Why seek the *yinan* herb in vain?
All things follow what was foreordained.

**Fifth Oracle – Great Auspice**
A flourishing legacy spans generations,
twin jade swallows take flight—an omen of fortune.
Lately, you’ve heard the wails of a newborn’s cry,
soon a mulberry bow will hang, shooting to the four directions.

**Sixth Oracle – Lower Auspice**
Jade is flawed, tiles are broken,
even on level ground, waves arise.
Had you not early invoked the gods’ power,
how could a lone boat cross treacherous shoals?

**Seventh Oracle – Uppermost Auspice**
A parasol tree shades the palace wall,
on its branches, the *luan* and *ju* birds already appear.
This time, you’ll obtain a being beyond the ordinary,
a child whose jade-like brilliance dawns boundless.

**Eighth Oracle – Medium Auspice**
Half-believing, half-doubting, the matter lingers,
yin and yang’s odd and even remain unknown.
Now I tell you plainly:
a lotus by the water unfurls a single petal.

**Ninth Oracle – Upper Auspice**
The *liujia* cycle has passed, the time is come,
morning and dusk, the lane will fill with joy.
As labor begins, take heed of both mother and child,
prepare the three fruits and *xiquian* coins without delay.

**Tenth Oracle – Lower-Medium Auspice**
Planting lotuses on stone yields no fruit,
cultivating chrysanthemums in water—how can they bloom?
Even if you seek the gods’ power,
the dream clearly showed a *hui*-serpent.

**Eleventh Oracle – Medium Auspice**
Spring enters the garden, rain and dew favor it,
the crabapple first blooms—a single fresh branch.
Do not say the *yinan* herb is vain,
this matter rests with Heaven’s leisure.

**Twelfth Oracle – Great Auspice**
The old is shed, renewal arises like a tripod’s restoration,
spring’s breeze and harmonious qi bring overflowing joy.
The *qilin* grasps the golden lock,
coming to grace your family as a treasure of the court.

**Thirteenth Oracle – Lower Auspice**
Creation’s flaws are unbearable,
why trouble to divine whether girl or boy?
Before noon or after, the news will come—
a burden of bright moon and clear wind.

**Fourteenth Oracle – Medium Auspice**
All things rest with the Great Potter’s wheel,
yet one must purify and inquire of the gods.
I tell you plainly: on Mid-Autumn night,
clouds scatter, revealing the jade sky’s single moon.

**Fifteenth Oracle – Uppermost Auspice**
A jade swallow clearly flies into your embrace,
why doubt with mortal sentiments?
Friends and kin, prepare gold and coins for celebration—
a fine scholar will crown the world’s groves.

**Sixteenth Oracle – Upper-Medium Auspice**
Lush auspicious qi overflows the courtyard,
good fortune aligns with Venus’s star.
One day, a noble son will surely be born—
do not disdain the humble home’s new addition.

**Seventeenth Oracle – Lower Auspice**
Fate’s pace is swift or slow by nature,
why weigh what is real or illusory?
Recall the sages’ words:
seeking fish where there are none yields no catch.

**Eighteenth Oracle – Medium Auspice**
Peach and apricot vie in fragrance,
yet not a branch of cinnamon appears.
Auspicious signs have not arrived—cease expectation,
and wait with patience for autumn’s time.

**Nineteenth Oracle – Medium Auspice**
Accumulate hidden virtue in obscurity,
orchids and irises gradually fill the courtyard.
Generation after generation, this hope endures—
why fret over the wasp’s adoption of the *mingling*?

**Twentieth Oracle – Lower Auspice**
A wisp of cloud veils the moon in darkest night,
flowers fall in the cold wind—no fruit forms.
Magpies perch together, crying as one,
fortune and misfortune remain indistinct.

**Twenty-First Oracle – Medium Auspice**
Lately, fortune’s course has been adverse,
idle talk of dragon colts and phoenix fledglings.
To ask of present blessings or misfortunes,
best perform good deeds for silent support.

**Twenty-Second Oracle – Medium Auspice**
To ask of the womb’s matter—there is cause:
a *hui*-serpent has repeatedly appeared in dreams.
One day, you’ll see her ride in a fish-shaped carriage,
no ordinary broom-and-dustpan woman.

**Twenty-Third Oracle – Upper-Medium Auspice**
Orchids and cinnamon exude fragrance beyond common blooms,
the Xie family’s garden henceforth enjoys fine light.
Do not say their fruit ripens late,
creation’s design is never in haste.

**Twenty-Fourth Oracle – Lower Auspice**
Abandoning plow and hoe, you guard the stump alone,
waiting for the rabbit—yet no rabbit comes.
Laugh at those who greedily gaze at the Mid-Autumn moon,
losing the luminous pearl in their dish.

**Twenty-Fifth Oracle – Medium Auspice**
Fruit trees, meeting spring, have sprouted,
further nourished by rain and dew to flourish.
The branch’s fine fruit awaits your harvest—
do not let the wind startle you.

**Twenty-Sixth Oracle – Upper Auspice**
The colorful phoenix hatches its young as the sun rises,
feathers gradually form patterns of literature.

**Twenty-Seventh Oracle – Medium Auspice**
This matter is no easy feat to reckon,
yet your family’s世泽 runs long and deep.

**Twenty-Eighth Oracle – Upper-Medium Auspice**
They laugh for days on end with boundless joy,
calling "a tile" when it should be "a jade scepter."
But if the newborn thrives like *Yi* of old,
no need to fear the bamboo mat or woven tray.

**Twenty-Ninth Oracle – Lower-Medium Auspice**
A house that heaps good deeds knows blessings overflow,
as one who dives for pearls indeed finds luminous treasure.
Yet strive to cultivate good works without cease—
rely on the powers of heaven to uphold your fortune.

**Thirtieth Oracle – Lower Auspice**
Yesterday’s dream of red blossoms adorning your frame,
today’s arrival here should not be doubted.
Clearly, your lingering doubts are resolved—
as the broom beside the door has long foretold.

**Thirty-First Oracle – Lower Auspice**
Why fret so ceaselessly from dawn to dusk?
Better to trust the Dao and let nature take its course.
Diving for pearls, the pearl remains unfound—
beware the river’s fire and the stone’s scorching skin.

**Thirty-Second Oracle – Upper Auspice**
Virtue in darkness silently lends its aid,
traversing rugged paths until level ground appears.
Soon you’ll summon the laborer from the fields,
early to hang the mulberry bow and catalpa arrows.

**Thirty-Third Oracle – Lower-Medium Auspice**
A bright moon illuminates the secluded chamber,
desires voiced, then dreams grow tangled and confused.
Do not sigh that your wishes go unfulfilled—
greater still is the unseen force that guides you.

**Thirty-Fourth Oracle – Upper-Medium Auspice**
When the time is ripe, affairs fall into place,
no need to burn incense and question heaven.
Heaven itself aligns with mortal wishes—
soon you’ll reclaim the fertile fields through your own strength.

**Thirty-Fifth Oracle – Lower Auspice**
Toiling in the fields, you yearn for autumn’s harvest,
yet know the weeds and chaff will choke the furrows.
From now on, tire not in vigilant tending—
beware the mischief of the two-tailed ox.

**Thirty-Sixth Oracle – Upper-Medium Auspice**
Gathering mountain fruit, you find jade uncut,
diving into waters, you retrieve the radiant pearl.
Prepare the jade-like fruit and bronze coins early—
lush blessings already fill your gate.

**Thirty-Seventh Oracle – Upper-Medium Auspice**
When fortune wanes, even true gold loses its luster;
when fortune turns, even ironwood blooms.
Now, joy upon joy unfolds—
no longer like before, when sighs were all in vain.

**Thirty-Eighth Oracle – Lower-Medium Auspice**
For thirty years, your fate has not aligned,
toiling in mind and body, yet reaping no reward.
One idle day, you wander to the Southern Sea—
a luminous pearl rests in your palm.

**Thirty-Ninth Oracle – Medium Auspice**
You stammer before others, unable to speak,
holding sweetness in your mouth, yet unwilling to swallow.
Auspicious matters drift like clouds—how can they be certain?
Only the quiet dawns and dusks remain.

**Fortieth Oracle – Lower Auspice**
Three worms gnaw at blood, their schemes manifold,
dark harm encroaches, and peace eludes you.
Even if flowers bloom and fruit sets,
the harvest will be unfit for consumption.

**Forty-First Oracle – Medium Auspice**
The sun’s crow spreads its wings toward due south—
this matter is clear, no need for doubt.
Hanging bells for swallows, both omens align,
yet still, you must pray to guard against peril.

**Forty-Second Oracle – Medium Auspice**
The succession of heirs lingers—do not guess,
for creation’s design was set long ago.
To discern the principle of hardness and softness,
last night, the yin essence flew into your embrace.

**Forty-Third Oracle – Upper-Medium Auspice**
Intent on planting flowers, yet the flowers do not bloom;
casually planting willows, the willows cast their shade.
Now, with the east wind’s lingering strength,
both planting willows and flowers bring contentment.

**Forty-Fourth Oracle – Upper-Medium Auspice**
Your noble lineage stretches far and wide,
phoenix chicks and dragon colts are yours to summon.
To know whether this will come soon or late,
wait no more than two days or three mornings.

**Forty-Fifth Oracle – Lower-Medium Auspice**
The Lord of Spring spreads warmth in due course,
fragrant scenes and flourishing things stir joy.
Yet you must seek the gods’ protection—
lest a hare’s crossing on level ground stirs a storm.

**Forty-Sixth Oracle – Medium Auspice**
Beneath the bamboo mat, atop the woven tray, you drowse,
in dreams, a snake transforms into a dragon.
This omen foretells the birth of a noble daughter—
a fish-shaped carriage and grand titles await the virtuous lady.

**Forty-Seventh Oracle – Upper-Medium Auspice**
Since ancient times, when yin reaches its peak, yang revives,
now, the noble one rejoices in the Dao’s flourishing.
The dream of the yellow tortoise’s song remains unfinished—
yet already, from the birthing mat, wails resound.

**Forty-Eighth Oracle – Upper Auspice**
This omen arises from the earth-marsh encounter,
at the appointed time, all things align with your heart.
For years, you envisioned the dream of bears and panthers—
today, sifting sand, you find gold in abundance.

**Forty-Ninth Oracle – Great Auspice**
Good fortune lies clearly before your eyes,
arranged like jade fruit and rhinoceros coins.
Who would dare mistake it for a common crow?
The sharpness of its horns and edges inspires awe.

**Fiftieth Oracle – Lower-Medium Auspice**
News is faint, the time uncertain,
yet you come here to divine your doubts.
Clearly, this is not the cassia of Eastern Grove—
the moon illuminates a branch of *tubie* blossoms.

**Fifty-First Oracle – Upper-Medium Auspice**
The sun climbs three poles high, spring mist dissipates,
green mountains stretch endlessly, waters flow serenely.
Fisherman, do not say no fish are to be found—
where none dwell, cast your hook elsewhere.

**Fifty-Second Oracle – Upper-Medium Auspice**
A pear’s form reveals a crimson snake,
divine favor descends upon your home.
One day, its jade-like horns will grow long—
prosperity for generations to come, a cause for pride.

**Fifty-Third Oracle – Upper Auspice**
The fleeting spring light has not yet passed,
yin and yang intertwine, their qi harmonized.
In the hall, guests gather for the birth feast,
vying to sing the *Xu Qing’s Two Sons* ode.

**Fifty-Fourth Oracle – Lower Auspice**
Sifting sand, no gold appears,
yet your schemes bring no satisfaction.
Go forth and seek the aid of unseen forces—
lest the stone’s skin and river’s fire assail you.

**Fifty-Fifth Oracle – Upper-Medium Auspice**
Layered cushions, lined tripods, a mansion’s halls—
none compare to having a son, where all is fulfilled.
Best of all is a piece of jade from Kun Mountain—
in the end, it all depends on ancestral fortune.

**Fifty-Sixth Oracle – Lower-Medium Auspice**
Your heart wavers between joy and alarm—
a promising affair, yet unclear in form.
Peaches and plums in the rear garden near fruition,
but fear the wind may shake them ere they ripen.

**Fifty-Seventh Oracle – Lower-Lower Auspice**
Gazing afar at the Yangtze’s endless flow,
reeds whisper autumn’s sigh in twilight’s glow.
Midnight’s chill stuns the fish to stillness deep—
the fisherman casts his golden hook in vain.

**Fifty-Eighth Oracle – Medium-Medium Auspice**
At dawn, the crow caws by the front pillar’s beam,
heralding jade-like branches sprouting by the eaves.
Yet more, unseen virtue shields and guards—
sparing you the birth-bed’s joy turned fright.

**Fifty-Ninth Oracle – Upper Auspice**
From goodness ever flows a hundred blessings,
the hall resounds with laughter, jade in hand.
Tomorrow brings yet more to boast—
a ring unearthed from roots reveals the Yang.

**Sixtieth Oracle – Upper-Medium Auspice**
The matter weighs upon your heart, you know it well,
ancestral virtue follows unseen, a silent swell.
If doves’ nests may yield noble hawks,
why doubt the tiger’s den might bear a leopard’s son?

**Sixty-First Oracle – Medium-Lower Auspice**
The road ahead is rugged, far from smooth,
mist and rain obscure the path to come.
Haste brings stumbles—why rush blindly so?
Better to wander, step by measured step.

**Sixty-Second Oracle – Lower Auspice**
Incense lit, teeth clicked, you pray to gods on high,
why toil so ceaselessly to sow your field of fortune?
If what you seek below comes to pass,
a red lotus shall bloom amid the flames.

**Sixty-Third Oracle – Lower-Lower Auspice**
The curtains rise to welcome spring’s return,
yet spring remains unclaimed by mortal hand.
A lotus planted on stone hopes for roots in vain—
wasted effort, heart and spirit spent.

**Sixty-Fourth Oracle – Medium Auspice**
Beyond the courtyard, spring arrives—sweep the green moss clean,
plant peaches and plums while the season is keen.
If the Lord of the East grants mortal desire,
they shall bloom anew, as they once did before.

*Xu Xian’s True Record, Scroll Two Concluded*
*Xu Xian’s True Record, Scroll Three*

**The Founding of the Lingji Palace in the Capital and the Erection of Its Stele**

In the fifteenth year of the Yongle reign, *dingyou* (1417), the Emperor decreed Minister Fang Bin and Commander Lin Guan to construct the Lingji Temporary Palace within the western part of Beijing’s inner city. To its east and west were built the *Qinmu Zhusheng* Halls. The flanking corridors housed the generals and their retinues, all modeled after the ancestral palace in Fujian. The work was completed on the fifteenth day of the ninth month that year. Later, due to negligence in maintaining its virtue, the palace fell into disrepair. In the autumn of the tenth year of *yimao* (1435), the Emperor again decreed the Ministry of Works and the eunuchs to expand and rebuild upon the original foundation, refining its scale and grandeur. On the fifteenth day of the first month in the first year of the Zhengtong reign, *bingchen* (1436), a stele was erected, and the rites of sacrifice were elevated beyond those of former times.

**Imperial Stele for the Restoration of the Hong’en Lingji Palace**

The Lingji Palace in the capital was established by Our Imperial Great-Grandfather, the Taizong Wen Emperor. His achievements surpassed those of antiquity, his benevolence blanketed the realm, and the flourishing of his governance remains unmatched. Yet even in his time, when Heaven and humanity responded in harmony and the hundred spirits manifested their efficacy, their hidden aid and manifest blessings—impossible to conceal—demanded reverent worship. Thus, in the *kun* quarter of the Forbidden City, this palace was built to enshrine the Two Xu Immortals. This follows the *Zhou* principle of "ordering all without omission," not merely for the sake of prayer and supplication.

The deities were descendants of the Southern Tang during the Five Dynasties. The elder was named Xu Zhizheng, and the younger, Xu Zhie. Their lineage, titles, meritorious deeds, and the details of their responsive manifestations were already recorded in the stele erected by Our Imperial Father during his restoration of the palace. Upon examining their lives, We observe: the deities’ innate endowments were both heroic and peerless, and they shared a single heart in their love of goodness. When stationed in Jinling, they soothed refugees, lightened taxes, and won the people’s reverence. Later, upon receiving orders to campaign in Min, they abhorred warfare. Wherever they went, they pacified and comforted the people, who surrendered at the mere rumor of their approach. Even those who rebelled in the mountains were dealt with by punishing only the ringleaders, while the rest were pardoned. Thus, the people held them in deep gratitude, erecting a shrine in their honor at the foot of Jinao Peak to express their devotion. Their benevolence had truly taken root in the hearts of the people.

Though the deities later departed this world, their spiritual essence did not fade. They descended in spirit upon this shrine, their divine brush and immortal slips leaving wondrous traces, and the people’s affairs grew ever more orderly. In times of flood, drought, pestilence, wind, fire, locusts, or other calamities, prayers were answered without fail. Those in dire peril, without heirs, or embroiled in battle who called upon the deities found their pleas met—countless instances defy enumeration.

From the Kaiyun era of the Later Jin, through the Jiaxi era of the Song when a temple was established and a name bestowed, to the Yuanzhen era of the Yuan when they were enfeoffed with titles such as *Jinque* and *Yueque* (Golden and Jade Towers) and honored as *Great Immortals* and *Supreme Immortals*, their numinous power had long been renowned in the region, though their glory had not yet reached its full splendor. In the fifteenth year of Our Imperial Great-Grandfather’s reign, he fell gravely ill, and no medicine proved effective. Someone spoke of the deities’ miraculous efficacy, and so he prayed with utmost sincerity. Indeed, a profound response manifested: through divine talismans and wondrous remedies, he recovered fully, the ancestral altars were secured, and the people found solace. The deities’ merit shone resplendently. Thus, grand and solemn rites of gratitude were established, sparing no effort in their magnificence.

Their titles were expanded with layered honors, their fame and virtue intertwined. The temple in Min was grandly renovated, and seasonal sacrifices, annual vestments, and attendants for sweeping were provided. In the capital, a temporary shrine was erected for their worship, bestowed the name *Hong’en Lingji* (Vast Grace and Numinous Aid)—this very palace. The invocations and sacrificial rites were unparalleled in their splendor. From then on, the deities’ awe-inspiring power blazed in the heavens, as radiant as the sun and moon, as manifest as wind and thunder. The four directions and ten thousand lands all gazed in reverence and veneration. The blessings they bestowed defy description—how magnificent!

Since then, successive sagely emperors have further honored their worship. In the early Zhengtong era, Our Imperial Father, the Yingzong Rui Emperor, once again restored the palace and elevated their titles to *True Lords*. Over fifty years have passed since then. Now, We have inherited the great enterprise of Our Ancestors, sheltered under the deities’ protective shade, and deeply reflect that Our devotion to their veneration may yet be insufficient. Thus, in the autumn of the *yisi* year of the Chenghua reign (1485), We commanded ministers within and without the court to oversee the work, gather materials, expand the original foundation, and add halls and corridors, ensuring utmost solidity and refinement. The following year, *bingwu* (1486), the project was completed: glazed tiles and gilded ornaments gleamed brilliantly, and the imperial regalia and ritual implements were meticulously arranged.

Thereupon, We bestowed exalted titles: the elder was named *Supreme Emperor of the Nine Heavens, Golden Tower, Grand Overseer of the Celestial Chiefs, Vast Grace and Numinous Aid, Benevolent and Illustrious*; the younger, *Supreme Emperor of the Nine Heavens, Jade Tower, Grand Overseer of the Celestial Warriors, Vast Grace and Numinous Aid, Benevolent and Vastly Serene*. This follows the Daoist scriptures, which state they originally held office in the Dipper Palace. The titles of their parents and consorts were also elevated in accordance with their former honors. A propitious day was chosen for the sacrificial announcement, and their numinous radiance shone forth. Our heart was gratified, and all agreed that this occasion demanded a record.

We reflect: the qi of Heaven and Earth is most numinous and unfathomable—this is the nature of the divine. Humans receive this qi to live. Those who, in life, possess wisdom, uprightness, and the ability to establish meritorious deeds for eternity, and in death, continue to manifest their numinous efficacy, bestowing boundless blessings—these, too, are called divine. Truly, they aid the primordial qi of Heaven and Earth and assist in their transformative nurturance. To enjoy grand titles, receive honorifics, and be enshrined for a hundred generations, enduring as long as Heaven and Earth—who could say this is undeserved?

Now that the deities’ abode has been renewed, their dragon chariots and cloud banners ascend and descend in stately procession, and fragrant wine and jade mats await their morning and evening enjoyment. May they silently regulate the transformative mechanisms of Heaven and Earth and universally bestow their vast blessings upon all living beings. Above, may they protect Our Sagely Mother with ten thousand years of longevity; in the middle, may they safeguard Our person, the heir apparent, and the imperial line for a hundred generations; below, may they grant ministers and the people the blessings of wealth, longevity, and well-being.

May the house and state endure ten thousand years of glory, and may the deities forever receive boundless offerings in return—this is Our deepest wish. Thus, We carve this stone and inscribe a poem:

Heaven-born, Huang Yu became a deity,
Mastering creation’s work, riding wind and cloud.
None below compare in aiding and benefiting all—
Who but these Two Perfected Ones could match such grace?
Born in the Five Dynasties, their talents unmatched,
They jointly governed key regions, laboring in pacification and tour.
First they crushed rebellion, purging foul vapors,
Yet spared those coerced, nurturing them with benevolence.
Their earnest kindness and love lingered among the people,
And on the southern slope of Mount Ao, their temple still stands.
Their numinous responses, sudden and wondrous, defy full recounting:
Prayers for drought brought rain; floods cleared at their behest.
They drove off locusts, extinguished fires, averted peril and ruin—
For a hundred years, their divine power has only grown more vibrant.
Alas! When Our August Ancestor fell gravely ill,
A hundred remedies failed, and the deities were consulted.
They bestowed talismanic medicine, boundlessly wondrous,
And upon taking it, his illness vanished in an instant.
Thus, rites of gratitude were elevated, the temple’s form renewed,
And honorific titles were conferred with solemn ceremony.
Successive sagely rulers continued these offerings without cease,
Morning incense and evening silk—how earnest their devotion!
We have borne the great mandate for over two decades,
And time and again, the deities’ protection has enabled Our reverent sacrifices.
Now the palace halls are repaired, rituals refined,
Majestic and resplendent, their honored place restored.
Auspicious mists and propitious vapors coil like dragons,
While manifold blessings descend in profusion.
May they guard this court for a thousand myriad springs,
And aid Us in extending blessings to posterity.
May they universally bestow upon the Four Seas longevity and wealth in equal measure—
For the deities’ supreme numen, their blessings ever flourish.
This inscription shall proclaim their glory forever, never to fade.
Composed in the twenty-second year of the Chenghua reign.

By decree: Eunuchs of the Inner Palace, Huang Shun and Chen Gui; Grand Guardian of the Heir Apparent and Marquis of Dingxi, Jiang Wan; Junior Guardian of the Heir Apparent and Minister of Works, Liu Zhao.

The Lingji Palace, built in the reign of Our Ancestors, is the place where the Two Perfected Ones of the Golden and Jade Towers are venerated. Since ascending the throne, We have repeatedly received the deities’ protection and dispatched officials to present offerings in gratitude. All have reported that the temple’s halls and storerooms are too cramped to befit their station. Each time We hear this, Our heart cannot rest. We hold that the Son of Heaven is the master of the hundred deities, and the worship of deities is the state’s great affair. How could We tolerate such a state for their abode?

Recently, We commanded Eunuch Wei Xing to inspect the site, and his findings matched the reports. Thus, We resolved to undertake a grand renovation. Drawing from the inner treasury’s gold and silk, and mobilizing the capital’s garrison troops and skilled artisans from the supervisory bureaus, We now issue this decree to Huang Shun, Chen Gui, Jiang Wan, and Liu Zhao, entrusting you with oversight of the project. The halls, corridors, side chambers, and walls must surpass their former scale. The statues, ritual vessels, and decorative paintings shall be entrusted to Wei Xing’s supervision, crafted according to proper standards and reported in due order.

You must carefully assess the quantity of materials required, ensuring their use is clear and without waste. The labor of artisans and workers must be balanced, neither overburdened nor idle, to prevent resentment. Strictly discipline the military overseers and artisan foremen, forbidding deceit or malpractice that might hinder the work. Should any violate these orders, they shall be punished according to the severity of their offense, or sent for trial and punishment, or reported in detail for Our disposition.

Having received this commission, you must collaborate wholeheartedly and exhaust your efforts, so that all may gladly contribute to the work, and every phase be sturdy and finely wrought. Only then can it accord with Our reverence for the divine and invite the convergence of abundant blessings—universally bestowed upon the state and endlessly upon ministers and people.

You shall respectfully uphold this decree, and not neglect it. Thus decreed.

On the twenty-fourth day of the seventh month in the twenty-first year of the Chenghua reign, under the imperial seal, the Emperor decrees and instructs all officials, military personnel, commoners, and persons of every rank:

Since ascending the throne, We have reverently upheld the worship of all deities enshrined in the ritual canon. How much more so for the Two August Emperors of the Golden and Jade Towers—whose temples were established and sacrifices offered by Our imperial great-forefather, the Taizong Wen Emperor—must Our devotion be all the more meticulous.

As the temple halls had grown humble and worn, We allocated funds, selected materials, and set deadlines, commanding ministers both within and beyond the court to supervise their reconstruction. After years of labor, the work is now complete. Its layout is as follows:

At the center stand the two main halls of the Mysterious Capital and Purple Palace, front and rear. Between them lies a traversing hall, with a pavilion before the rear hall. To the left and right are the Halls of the Boundless and the Spiritually Manifest. Arrayed before and behind, east and west, are the four halls of Majestic Emptiness, Illuminated Revelation, Manifest Blessing, and Lofty Mystery, each flanked by painted corridors.

Before the halls stands the Great Portal of Manifest Majesty, with two side gates to the east and west. Four stele pavilions, two bell-and-drum towers, and two glazed-brick paper-offering towers stand in front. Further ahead is the Celestial Pivot Gate, also with side gates to the east and west. Beyond lies the mountain gate, inscribed *Hong’en Lingji Palace*. Flanking it are side gates, within which stand two cloud-board and bell pavilions, two banner poles, two well pavilions, two gatehouses, two divine storehouses, and one kitchen.

The Dharma hall, Daoist quarters, and abbot’s chambers, along with their eastern and western wings, total over three hundred and fifty bays. The entire complex is encircled by a sturdy wall, measuring eighty-three zhang and five chi in length, and fifty-seven zhang and eight chi in breadth.

Outside the mountain gate, the *Penglai* and *Langyuan* archways stand facing each other to the east and west. To the south, a high wall extends approximately fifty-seven zhang. Beyond this wall lies the *Peach Blossom Spring of Lingji Hall*, with its thatched halls and auxiliary chambers, also enclosed by a wall.

All ritual banners, pennants, liturgical instruments, and furnishings required for worship are now fully prepared. This is truly sufficient to honor the luminous spirits of the Two Emperors in heaven and to fulfill Our duty of continuing the reverent devotion of Our imperial great-forefather.

We hereby issue this decree for its protection and appoint the eunuch Wei Xing to inspect the site regularly. He shall supervise the resident clergy, ensuring that the assigned households maintain constant sweeping to keep the premises spotless. All persons are strictly forbidden from entering carelessly, lest they show disrespect or cause damage. Livestock must not be released within the grounds, nor may any act of violence, bullying of the Daoist community, or theft of ritual implements be tolerated.

The nine qing and seventy-four mu of land in Jiahe Village, Wanping County—granted during the Xuande reign—shall remain under the temple’s management to provide for incense and offerings. No one may encroach upon it. Those who violate these orders shall face punishment according to the severity of their offense: minor infractions will be met with disciplinary measures, while grave violations will be reported for trial and prosecution, with no pardon granted.

Let this be known.

On the fifteenth day of the eighth month in the twenty-first year of the Chenghua reign:
