*Ritual Regulations for Sacrificial Offerings*
Sacrificial animals for imperial rites.

Two altars in the Main Hall.
For each altar:
- One calf
- Ten bundles of reeds
- Ten [omitted item]
- One vessel of plain broth
- Two vessels of mixed broth
- Millet
- Sorghum
- Rice
- Fine millet
- Two bolts of silk
- Three goblets
- Wine

Four altars in the Hall of Harmonious Kinship and Life-Granting.
For each altar:
- One sheep
- One pig
- Eight bamboo baskets
- Eight [omitted item]
- Two vessels of mixed broth
- Millet
- Sorghum
- Rice
- Fine millet
- Two bolts of silk
- Three goblets
- Wine

Ten altars in total for the Seven Marshals, one Earth God, and two Examination Success Deities.
For each altar:
- One sheep
- One pig
- Three bamboo baskets
- Millet
- Sorghum
- Two goblets
- One vessel of wine

Two altars for the Multitude of Deities.
For each altar:
- One sheep
- One pig
- Three bamboo baskets
- Twelve [omitted item] cups
- Ten wine cups
- One vessel of wine

*Diagram of Vegetarian Offerings for Imperial Sacrifices*
Six altars in total for the Main Hall and the Hall of Harmonious Kinship and Life-Granting.
Twelve altars in total for the Seven Marshals, one Earth God, two Examination Success Deities, and the Multitude of Deities.
For each altar:
- Ritual officiant

Proceeding to the ablution station, the officiant inserts the ritual tablet, pours water, presents the towel, withdraws the tablet, and takes position.

*Welcoming the Deities*
Bow deeply, prostrate, rise; prostrate, rise; prostrate, rise; prostrate, rise; stand upright.

*Offering Incense*
Approach, kneel, insert the tablet, present incense, withdraw the tablet, prostrate, rise; kneel, insert the tablet, present incense, withdraw the tablet, prostrate, rise; stand upright, return to position.

*Presenting Silk*
Approach, kneel, lay down the tablet, present silk, withdraw the tablet, prostrate, rise; kneel, insert the tablet, present silk, withdraw the tablet, prostrate, rise; stand upright, return to position.

*Offering Sacrificial Animals*
For vegetarian offerings, declare: "Presenting the offering."
Approach, kneel, insert the tablet, present the sacrificial animal, withdraw the tablet, prostrate, rise; kneel, insert the tablet, present the sacrificial animal, withdraw the tablet, prostrate, rise; stand upright, return to position.

*Performing the First Libation*
Approach, kneel, insert the tablet, present the goblet, withdraw the tablet, prostrate, rise; kneel, insert the tablet, present the goblet, withdraw the tablet, prostrate, rise; stand upright, proceed to the prayer-reading position and kneel.
All officials kneel.
Read the prayer, prostrate, rise; prostrate, rise; prostrate, rise; prostrate, rise.
Stand upright, return to position.

*Performing the Second Libation*
Approach, kneel, insert the tablet, present the goblet, withdraw the tablet, prostrate, rise; kneel, insert the tablet, present the goblet, withdraw the tablet, prostrate, rise; stand upright, return to position.

*Performing the Final Libation*
Approach, kneel, insert the tablet, present the goblet, withdraw the tablet, prostrate, rise; kneel, insert the tablet, present the goblet, withdraw the tablet, prostrate, rise; stand upright, return to position.

*Farewelling the Deities*
Bow deeply, prostrate, rise; prostrate, rise; prostrate, rise; prostrate, rise; stand upright.
The prayer-reading official carries the prayer, the silk-presenting official carries the silk; both proceed to the burial site.

*Observing the Burial*
Ritual concludes.
Officials are dispatched to conduct the sacrifice.

**Annual Sacrificial Offerings with Animal Sacrifices**
Once annually, with the date selected in mid-first month. Six altars are prepared in the Main Hall and the Hall of Harmonious Longevity. Each altar comprises: seven Marshal deities, one Earth God, two Deities of Scholastic Success, and two Assorted Deities—twelve altars in total.

**Annual Vegetarian Offerings**
Fourteen times yearly, with four additional offerings on the auspicious days of the Perfected Lord and Immortal Consorts. For this altar, silk is used. On the Lantern Festival, Eighth Day of the Fourth Month, Dragon Boat Festival, Double Ninth Festival, Mid-Autumn Festival, Laba Festival, and Beginning of Spring—seven occasions—seasonal foods are added to the offerings. On the Winter Solstice, New Year’s Day, and the Sage’s Birthday—three occasions—only the standard offerings are presented. Six altars are prepared in the Main Hall and the Hall of Harmonious Longevity. Each altar comprises: seven Marshal deities, one Earth God, two Deities of Scholastic Success, and two Assorted Deities—twelve altars in total.

The ritual protocol remains as above, except that on the day of inserting the tablet, the *zhi* jade is covered. No silk is offered, nor is silk presented. Upon the conclusion of the vegetarian sacrifice, Daoist priests perform music and chant scriptures.

**Presiding Officials**
For the Sage’s Birthday, auspicious days (one occasion), Winter Solstice, and New Year’s Day—seven occasions—the Duke or Marquis of the Main Hall, or the principal official of the Ministry of Rites in the Hall of Harmonious Longevity, serves as the chief officiant. For the Lantern Festival, Eighth Day of the Fourth Month, Dragon Boat Festival, Double Ninth Festival, Mid-Autumn Festival, Laba Festival, and Beginning of Spring—seven occasions—the secondary principal official of the Ministry of Rites presides.

**Monthly and Seasonal Offerings**
On the first and fifteenth of each month, as well as during the four seasonal clothing changes, vegetarian offerings are presented. Six altars are prepared in the Main Hall and the Hall of Harmonious Longevity. Each altar comprises: seven Marshal deities, one Earth God, two Deities of Scholastic Success, and two Assorted Deities—twelve altars in total. The ritual protocol remains as above, except that no silk is offered; only offerings are presented. The chief officiant is an official of this abbey.

**Incense and Lamps**
Supplied by the Imperial Household Department, on the first and fifteenth of each month—two occasions per month—each time comprising:
- Twelve sticks of descending incense
- Three *jin* each of sandalwood and powdered descending incense
- Fifty *jin* of horse-teeth incense
- Three *jin* of ground incense (one *liang* of earth)
- Red candles, each weighing one *jin*: twelve pairs
- Red candles, each weighing half a *jin*: twenty-four pairs
- Two hundred *jin* of lamp oil

**Monthly Supplies from the Designated Depot**
Once monthly:
- Seven hundred *jin* of charcoal
- Three hundred charcoal cakes
- Three thousand *jin* of firewood

**Prayer Text for the Imperial Sacrifice**

On the fourth day of the eleventh month, *dingwei*, in the cyclical year *gengxu*, of the sixteenth year of the Yongle reign (16 November 1418), the Emperor respectfully offers sacrifice to the **Perfected Lords of Vast Grace, Sovereigns of the Nine Heavens**:

**Great Immortal of the Golden Portal of the Nine Heavens, Illuminator of the Dao, Attainer of Virtue, Manifest in Wondrous Efficacy, Vast in Salvation, Pure and Subtle, Penetrating the Mysteries, Void and Marvelous, Compassionate and Benevolent, Protector of the State and Shelter of the People**;

**Supreme Immortal of the Jade Portal of the Nine Heavens, Propagator of Transformation, Upholder of the Teachings, Radiant in Spirit, Boundless in Aid, Lofty and Luminous, Vast and Serene, Profound and Tranquil, Marvelously Responsive, Benevolent and Merciful, Assistant to the State and Guardian of the People**.

The prayer declares:

O Perfected Ones, your Dao is wondrous, your virtue profound, your merits towering, your deeds illustrious. Enthroned among the Supreme Immortals, you preside over the Nine Heavens, transcending the sacred and entering the numinous. You propagate divine blessings, assist the state, and succor all beings.

Recently, We fell gravely ill, and though myriad remedies were tried, none proved efficacious. Yet, by your turning of the wheel of transformation and your silent protection, you stood by Us day and night. You bestowed sacred talismans and dispensed the wondrous medicines of celestial physicians, reviving the dying and restoring the stricken. Thus, this enfeebled body, once perilously close to ruin, was swiftly stabilized; this deep-seated malady, once entrenched, was wholly dispelled, and health was restored.

In reverence, We contemplate your virtue—vast as heaven, deep as earth.

Deeply engraved upon Our heart and bones, how could We dare forget? Now, with grand offerings of the finest sacrifice, fragrant silks, and seasonal robes, We come before the Divine to render thanks. May you deign to accept and witness Our sincerest devotion, partaking of these offerings.

Moreover, on the nineteenth day of the first month, the cyclical day *jiazi*, in the seventeenth year of the Yongle reign, the year *jihai*, the Emperor offers sacrifice to the **Nine Heavens Golden Portal Illuminating Dao and Manifesting Virtue Great Immortal, Wondrously Responsive, Vastly Beneficent, Compassionate and Kind, Protecting the State and Sheltering the People, Vastly Merciful Perfected Lord**; and to the **Nine Heavens Jade Portal Proclaiming Transformation and Upholding the Teachings Supreme Immortal, Radiantly Manifest, Vastly Beneficent, Lofty and Serene, Profoundly Tranquil, Wondrously Responsive, Benevolent and Kind, Assisting the State and Aiding the People, Vastly Merciful Perfected Lord**.

We declare: Recently, We have conducted the **Grand Register Dao Offering**, performing the rites to extol and present Our late father, the August Emperor, and Our late mother, the August Empress, universally praying for blessings upon all beings under heaven and delivering all departed spirits. Humbly, We beseech the Vastly Merciful Perfected Lords to convey Our supplications to the Supreme Mystery, that Our filial piety may be modestly expressed, extending to both the manifest and the hidden, all receiving harmony and aid.

We reflect that the Vastly Merciful Perfected Lords’ Dao is wondrous, their virtue profound, their divine transformations unfathomable. Their numinous radiance blazes forth, silently operating in resonant response. Thus, the Highest Deities are moved to manifest, and the Host of Sages deign to attend. Auspicious clouds and propitious lights repeatedly display their five-colored omens. White cranes and azure simurghs truly harmonize with the responses of the hundred spirits. Longevity banners form from colored streamers, while the incense of sacred rites envelops the altar. In reverence, We recall Our late father, the August Emperor...

The late Empress’s celestial consolation and joy are truly the numinous guidance of the Vastly Merciful Perfected Lords. In this, heaven and humanity rejoice as one, and far and near alike receive grace. Our heart is filled with boundless gratitude. Now that the rites of abstinence are complete, We humbly present plain offerings to report and give thanks at the sacred precinct. May the ancient favor persist, and may the Perfected Lords deign to regard Our sincere devotion. May they accept and partake.

Moreover, on the twenty-seventh day of the fourth month in the year *jihai* of the seventeenth year of the Yongle reign (a *xinchou* day), the Emperor offers sacrifice to the **Vastly Merciful Perfected Lord of the Nine Heavens’ Golden Portal, Illuminating the Dao and Manifesting Virtue, Great Immortal of Universal Salvation, Pure and Subtle, Void and Wondrous, Compassionate and Benevolent, Protector of the State and Shelter of the People**; and to the **Vastly Merciful Perfected Lord of the Nine Heavens’ Jade Portal, Propagating Transformation and Upholding the Teachings, Supreme Immortal of Radiant Salvation, Lofty and Serene, Profound and Mysterious, Wondrously Responsive, Benevolent and Merciful, Assistant to the State and Guardian of the People**, proclaiming:

Recently, the Vastly Merciful Perfected Lords conducted the **Grand Register Fast** at the Sacred Salvation Palace in Fujian, offering libations to the Supreme Perfected Ones and praying on Our behalf. We reflect that their divine transformations are unfathomable, their Dao-power vast and profound, moving the Highest Deities to respond with favor and the Supreme Mystery to regard with delight. Auspicious clouds and propitious mists repeatedly displayed their five-colored omens. White cranes and azure simurghs arrived in succession over many days. The divine spirits descended in an instant, manifesting extraordinary signs. The imperial realm enjoys the stability of reinforced foundations, and Our person has received the gift of renewed life. May safety, longevity, and peace be preserved, and may life endure in well-being. Their profound virtue and deep grace are as boundless as heaven and earth. Engraved upon Our heart and bones, how could We ever dare forget?

Herewith the completion of the Daoist rites, We reverently present incense, silk offerings, and ritual provisions at the palace to render thanks. May the Most High deign to accept and look favorably upon Our humble devotion. May They be pleased to receive.

Moreover,
On the twenty-fifth day of the third month in the year *jihai* of the *Yongle* reign’s seventeenth cycle (the day *jisi* following the new moon of *yisi*), the Imperial Grandson respectfully proclaims to the
**Nine Heavens’ Golden Portal, Illuminated Dao and Penetrating Virtue, Great Immortal of Manifest Numinosity, Vast Salvation, Pure Subtlety, Cavernous Mystery, Void Wonder, Wondrous Response, Compassionate Grace, Protector of the State and Shelter of the People, Vastly Benevolent Perfected Lord**,
and to the
**Nine Heavens’ Jade Portal, Propagating Transformation and Upholding the Teachings, Supreme Immortal of Radiant Numinosity, Vast Salvation, Lofty Clarity, Vast Serenity, Void Profundity, Wondrous Response, Benevolent Grace, Assistant of the State and Guardian of the People, Vastly Benevolent Perfected Lord**:
At the command of Our Grandfather the Emperor, We have come to pay homage. With reverence, We present sacrificial animals, fine wine, and various offerings at the palace to make offering to the Vastly Benevolent Perfected Lords. May They deign to regard this.

May They be pleased to receive.

**Deputy Officials Sent to Offer Sacrifice**
**Completion of the Capital Temple**

On the fifteenth day of the ninth month in the fifteenth year of the *Yongle* reign, a certain official was dispatched to offer sacrifice, saying:
The new temple of the Divine has now been completed. Having chosen an auspicious day, We install the Divine Presence within. May the numinous power of the Divine shine resplendently, and may the incense fire flourish abundantly. May Their blessings bestow abundant protection, and Their grace extend to all the people. For ten thousand years and evermore, may They protect Our state and family.

May They be pleased to receive.
**Respectfully offered on this auspicious dawn.**

**Golden Portal, the seventeenth day of the ninth month.**
**Jade Portal, the fifteenth day of the seventh month.**

On the ___ day of the ___ month of the ___ year, a certain official was dispatched to offer sacrifice, saying:
The Divine has received Its charge from the Nine Heavens, and in awe of Its numinous power descends to the earth. Spreading Its protection over the common people, It shields and assists the state. The Dao is wondrous, Its virtue profound; Its merits towering, Its deeds illustrious. Now, on this reverent occasion of the Perfected Lord’s birth, We present this plain offering in sacrifice. May the Divine deign to regard and know. May It be pleased to receive.

**Bestowal of Sacred Titles**

On the seventeenth day of the eleventh month of the present year, a certain official was dispatched to offer sacrifice, saying:
The Divine has rendered service to Our person, and We have already bestowed a title upon It. Yet the rites of posthumous honor for the Divine’s kin remain; it is fitting to confer special titles:
The father, Prince Qi, is granted the title *Loyal and Martial Illuminating Perfected Person*.
The mother, née Tian, is granted the title *Benevolent and Longevous Pure and Good Immortal Consort*.
The first consort, née Xu, is granted the title *Yielding and Assisting Benevolent and Responsive Immortal Consort*.
The second consort, née Tao, is granted the title *Kindly Assisting Compassionate and Reverent Serene Immortal Consort*.
We hereby announce this. May It be pleased to receive.

**Preservation and Construction**

On the thirteenth day of the first month in the sixteenth year of the *Yongle* reign, a certain official was dispatched to offer sacrifice, saying:
In the construction of the palaces of Beijing, soldiers, commoners, laborers, and artisans all gladly hasten to their tasks and attend to their work, undeterred by toil. We bear this in mind and have not forgotten it for even a moment. Yet the project is vast, and during the course of labor, some may not receive their meals at the proper time, or find rest in suitable quarters. Some endure the cold, braving frost, rising early and retiring late. All seven emotions may be stirred, and illness may arise. We have already commanded physicians to prepare medicines for their care, but human effort has its limits, and the aid of medicine is slight. Without the support of the Divine, how could such great benevolence be attained? May It be pleased to receive.

May the Divine, in Its great virtue, aid the state and shelter the people. We humbly rely upon Its manifest majesty to silently bestow protection, that illness may not arise, noxious qi be silently dispelled, and all attain health and peace, forever enjoying boundless blessings. May the Divine perceive Our present intent. May It deign to accept.

**Sacred Anniversary**
On the seventeenth day of the fourth month of this year, We dispatched an official to offer sacrifice, saying:
In Its virtue and power, the Divine has achieved towering, illustrious deeds. Formerly, when Our person was afflicted by illness, the Divine silently exerted Its numinous efficacy, safeguarding and shielding Us, bringing Us to this day. Now, on the morning of Our natal anniversary, We specially dispatch this plain offering in sacrifice. May the Divine perceive it. May It deign to accept.

**Enfeoffment and Temple Proclamation**
On the twenty-seventh day of the twelfth month of the sixteenth year of the Yongle reign, We dispatched an official to make this solemn proclamation:
In Its vast virtue and luminous Dao, the Divine has rendered illustrious service to both realms, its life’s work dedicated to sheltering the people. It assists the transformations of Heaven and Earth, wards off calamities, and repels misfortune, so that all things rely upon It for tranquility. Formerly, when Our person was afflicted by illness, all remedies proved ineffectual. The Divine, turning the wheel of great transformation, greatly manifested Its numinous favor. Morning and evening, It silently protected Our person. It bestowed upon Us divine talismans and celestial physicians’ wondrous medicines, so that Our enfeebled body, once imperiled, was restored to safety; Our deep-seated ailments, once entrenched, were wholly cast off and returned to health. In Its vast deliverance from dire straits, We obtained renewal of life. Our heart is deeply inscribed with gratitude—how could We dare forget? We have already conferred upon the Divine a title of enfeoffment to express Our sentiments. Yet day and night, Our devotion remains earnest, and We find this still insufficient. Now, We further confer these titles:

*Celestial Golden Portal of the Nine Heavens, Illuminated Dao and Penetrating Virtue, Great Immortal Manifesting Numinous and Universal Salvation, Pure and Subtle, Void and Wondrous, Compassionate and Benevolent, Protector of the State and Shelter of the People, True Lord of Vast Grace;*

*Celestial Jade Portal of the Nine Heavens, Propagating Transformation and Upholding the Teachings, Supreme Immortal of Illustrious Numinosity and Vast Salvation, Lofty and Luminous, Vast and Serene, Profound and Wondrous, Benevolent and Compassionate, Auxiliary of the State and Protector of the People, True Lord of Vast Grace.*

Thus do We respond to Its boundless favor and slightly extend Our repayment.

We offer thanks and earnestly beseech Your luminous presence to deign to witness Our humble devotion. On the propitious dawn of the Immortal Consort: the thirteenth day of the first month in the State of Jing, and the seventeenth day of the seventh month in the State of Wei. On this day, month, and year, We dispatch [such-and-such] official to present offerings at the altar of the Immortal Consort, declaring:

Of the Divine, Your virtue unites with the utmost truth, Your merit pervades the mysterious transformation. Your rank ascends among the immortals, Your office is received from the Nine Heavens. Sheltering and nurturing all beings, Your manifest responses are ever evident. On this, Your sacred birth day, We reverently present pure offerings in sacrifice—may the Divine deign to accept them. May You graciously partake.

To convey the intent of the Supreme Daoist Ritual, We respectfully adhere to the Sacred Decree:

Our Imperial Father, the Grand Progenitor Emperor, received the Mandate of Heaven, governing the vast realm. He established enduring principles for ten thousand generations and inaugurated the grand enterprise of Great Peace. Our Imperial Mother, the Filial and Compassionate Grand Empress, jointly labored in the founding, aiding through hardship and assisting in the myriad affairs, thereby perfecting the inner governance.

We, relying on the protection of Heaven and Earth and the numinous favor of Our Imperial Father and Imperial Mother, have succeeded to the great inheritance, reverently upholding the ancestral legacy. Deeply mindful of the arduous burden We bear, We have yet to fully repay the debt of life bestowed. Yet, as They have long since ascended, We reflect...

Where Their ascent and descent seem ever-present, We now undertake offerings and exaltations, specially extending Our grief and longing. Considering the vastness of the Four Seas, the teeming multitudes of people and creatures—all equally embraced by the vast generative power of the Great Creation—We feel gratitude and reliance upon the Mysterious Heavens that govern and sustain.

Desires for wealth, for nobility, for longevity—these are common to every human heart. Yet the cycles of rain and sunshine, of warmth and cold, remain unfathomable in the heavens’ timing. How much more so the misfortunes of flood and drought, the unpredictability of famine, or the sudden onset of plague and pestilence? When even a single being finds no peace, We hold Ourself personally accountable.

Deeply mindful of all within the embrace of Heaven and Earth, of the numinous spirits both hidden and manifest—some clinging to grass and trees without refuge, others howling to the moon and wind without shelter—We extend Our concern even to the multitudes of flying, walking, and creeping creatures, to the humble beings born of womb, egg, moisture, or transformation, long sunk in suffering with no means of deliverance.

Thus, on the ninth day of the first month in the seventeenth year of the Yongle reign, We commanded the Daoist assembly at the Hong’en Lingji Palace to perform the seven-day, seven-night *Yanxi Pudu Luotian Grand Offering*, comprising one thousand two hundred altar stations. Reverently beseeching the *Nine Heavens Golden Portal Illuminated Dao and Manifest Virtue Great Immortal, Universally Beneficent, Subtly Responsive, Compassionate and Gracious Protector of the Realm and Shelter of the People, Hong’en Perfected Lord*; and the *Nine Heavens Jade Portal Propagating Transformation and Upholding the Dao Supreme Immortal, Radiantly Manifest, Vastly Beneficent, Lofty and Serene, Profoundly Tranquil, Wondrously Responsive, Benevolent and Gracious Supporter of the Realm and Guardian of the People, Hong’en Perfected Lord*—We lay forth Our sincerity before the Supreme Mystery, modestly expressing Our filial devotion.

We humbly pray for wind in harmony and rain in season, that all directions may reap abundant harvests year after year; for the realm’s prosperity and the people’s peace, that the Four Seas may ascend to the realm of longevity. May the deliverance of the hidden and the manifest be universal, and distant and near alike receive grace.

Prostrate, We beseech the Mysterious Heavens to witness and the divine powers to magnify. May all beings bask in the transforming virtue of the Dao, and may the august numen of the imperial ancestors shine forth, bestowing deliverance and grace alike. May the great earth flourish in springtime, and all living things receive blessing.

Thus decreed. Officials are appointed to conduct the sacrifices.

The temple official Zeng Chensun, originally of the Zunyi Ward in Fuqing County, had his father Quan marry into the Chen family of Jishan Ward in Min County, where Chensun was born and subsequently registered as a resident. In the *dingchou* year of the Hongwu reign of the Great Ming, he first wielded the divine brush, divining talismans, medicines, geomancy, and fortunes with unfailing efficacy. His reputation reached the imperial court. In the *bingshen* year of the Yongle reign, envoys were dispatched to summon the spirit. In secret supplications for affairs of state, his responses proved infallible, and the more he was revered, the more potent his numen became.

On the eighteenth day of the fifth month in the *jihai* year of the Yongle reign, he was bestowed with official robes and sashes, appointed to guard the temple and conduct sacrifices, with a monthly stipend of five *shi* of rice. An emissary was sent to bring his family together. Thereafter, official quarters were constructed to the west of the temple for his residence.

Officials appointed to conduct sacrifices:
- One eunuch from the Inner Court
- One Daoist official from the Directorate of Daoist Registrations
- Commander Lin Guan of the Embroidered Uniform Guard
- Bailiff Liu Zhen
- Attendant Guards Guo Tai and Liao Zhen

Selection of Daoist incense-burners: Initially, twelve were chosen, matching the number at the ancestral temple in Fujian. Later, additional selections were made as needed.

Daoist officiants:
Zhang Shouzhen, Wu Ximin, Zhang Yining, Cao Chengzu, Yin Yizheng, Guo Tong, Yao Kedao, Zhang Fuyan, Shi Daoyi, Cui Shouyi, Wu Dezhong, Lu Shangwen, Ni Zhengdao, Lou Jingzhong, Ge Zizhen, Sun Bendao, Lu Huncheng, Zhang Yousong, Lü Daocun, Yang Yuchun, Fan Yunshan, Luo Zhongshan, Lü Zhizhong, Zheng Shouqing, Zhu Daofang, Chen Chongmu, Zhu Chongxian, Dao Hong, Hu Wen, Shi Qing’an, Han De, Zhu Dao’an, Zhou Zongdao, Qian Yongchang, Jin Yining.

Assigned temple servitors:
Miao Hu: Su Gui, Wang Chun, Wang Xing, Liu Zheng, Xi Xian, Gao Cheng, Ding Wang, Zhang Fu, Zhang Zhen, Wei Zhen, Niu Song, Yang Xin, Zhao Li, Zhang Bin, Dong Hui, Lu Gui, Su Neng, Li Gang, Fan Yong, Liu Xing.

The above twenty households, on the first day of the tenth month in the twenty-second year of the Yongle reign, were recorded under Imperial Edict No. 45,300. Eunuch Ruan Yi transmitted the sacred decree: "The twenty temple servitors, including Liu Yuan, of the Sacred Relief Palace shall perpetually maintain the temple’s cleanliness, exempted from all miscellaneous corvée labor. Each household may open a shop at their doorstep. All other miscellaneous duties shall be entirely remitted." Respectfully received.

By imperial decree, the aforementioned exemptions shall be upheld in accordance with precedent. Respectfully noted.

*Xu Zhenlu, Volume Four*
*Sacred Relief Palace of Fujian*

The temple’s stele was erected on the twenty-eighth day of the first month in the fifteenth year of the Yongle reign. By sacred imperial command: Commanders Tong Jun and Xu Sheng, Vice Censor-in-Chief, were ordered to oversee its reconstruction. All required artisans, laborers, timber, bricks, tiles, and other materials were to be procured by the Ministry of Works through official correspondence. Respectfully noted.

Ministry of Works Document No. 4,256: The provincial administration was instructed, in conjunction with the provincial and surveillance commissions, to ensure the reconstruction was carried out with meticulous order. Construction commenced on the twenty-sixth day of the fourth month of the same year and was completed on the sixth day of the fifth month of the following year. Subsequently, a stone stele and its tortoise pedestal were quarried in Nanjing, transported by sea, and erected with the aid of ten thousand laborers.

Officials entrusted with supervising the construction:
Eunuch Zhang Da.
Commissioned Officer Zhang Gui of the Embroidered Uniform Guard.
Zhou Ne, Vice Minister of the Court of Imperial Sacrifices.
Tong Jun, Commander of Fujian.
Wei Yong, Commissioned Commander of the Fujian Regional Military Commission.
Zu Shu, Right Administration Vice Commissioner of the Fujian Provincial Administration Commission.
Xu Sheng, Vice Censor-in-Chief of the Fujian Surveillance Commission.
Officials of the subordinate prefectures and counties.
Chen Letu.
Xie Shangzhen offered incense in reverence.

I humbly reflect that the noble lineage of the Southern Tang once flourished among the eastern gentry. From youth, he immersed himself in poetry and books, ever observing fasts and upholding precepts. In maturity, he bore titles of nobility, diligently accumulating goodness to establish merit. His military command won renown for its might, and wielding the battle-axe, he pacified malevolent forces. His will held fast to steadfast integrity, and his person embodied the name of loyalty and filial piety. Though stabilizing the state and pacifying the people were not his appointed tasks, he dared not presume to accept the honors of a royal temple’s offerings.

Moreover, devoid of omens to sway men, who would deem him enlightened and sagely? Yet in rescuing the imperiled and aiding the distressed, he embodied the Supreme’s love for life. Responding to stimuli with timely efficacy, he assisted the Mysterious and True in their transformative work. Who could have foreseen that ascending the exalted ranks would elevate him beyond mortal bounds to the ranks of immortals? Bestowed with the title of *Zhenren* and lavished with the august name of the Golden Palace, he was entrusted with warding off calamities and averting disasters, unworthily assuming the governance of the Seven Min lands. In amassing auspiciousness and gathering blessings, he dared aspire to the numinous spirits of the Five Peaks.

May the fragrant incense endure for ten thousand years, and may this day witness the convergence of wind and cloud. Profoundly indebted to the sagely favor’s cherished regard, he now renews his countenance in grandeur. Radiant blossoms unite in splendor, harmonizing in concord. Robes and crowns remain as though he were present, and rites are once more fully prepared. The entire household is honored by the imperial commendation, and kinfolk are graced with extraordinary favor.

Your servant has reverently received the title: *Qingwei Dongxuan Chongxu Miaogan Cihui Huguo Bimin Hong’en Zhenjun*. His wife, Lady Xu, has been honored with the title *Zhenying Xianfei*. His younger brother has been enfeoffed as *Gaoming Hongjing Chongzhan Miaoying Renhui Fuguo Youmin Hong’en Zhenjun*. His brother’s wife, Lady Tao, has been honored with the title *Gongjing Xianfei*. His father has been enfeoffed as *Yiliang Zhenjun*. His mother, Lady Tian, has been honored with the title *Shushan Xianfei*.

Such profound grace, like a torrential downpour, flows entirely from the boundless generosity of the Great Creation. Day and night, I stand in awe and shame, unable to requite it. I humbly lay bare my sincerest devotion, offering solemn gratitude to the Most High. May the sacred person be safeguarded, and his celestial longevity further extended. May the imperial throne flourish, steadfast as bedrock. May winds be gentle and rains timely, yielding abundant harvests. May rivers run clear and seas remain calm, ushering in eternal peace and harmony. May sun and moon shine together, securing the imperial realm for ten thousand generations. May heaven and earth nurture all, gathering every blessing for the multitudes.

I pray that my earnest devotion be beheld from above, and that the wondrous Dao be invoked to bestow its blessings. The sagely intent has thus renewed the temple’s visage. Twin blossoms unite in radiance, harmonizing in perfect accord. Robes and crowns remain as though he were present, and rites are once more fully prepared. Every household is honored by the imperial commendation, and kinfolk are graced with extraordinary favor.

Your servant has reverently received the title: *Qingwei Dongxuan Chongxu Miaogan Hui Huguo Bimin Hong’en Zhenjun*. His wife, Lady Xu, has been honored with the title *Zhenying Xianfei*. His younger brother has been enfeoffed as *Gaoming Hongjing Chongzhan Miaoying Zaihui Hanguo Jun*. His brother’s wife, Lady Tao, has been honored with the title *Gongjing Xianfei*. His father has been enfeoffed as *Yiliang Zhenjun*. His mother, Lady Tian, has been honored with the title *Shushan Xianfei*.

Such profound grace, like a torrential downpour, flows from the convergence of wind and cloud on this day. Deeply indebted to the boundless generosity of the Great Creation, I stand in awe day and night, unable to requite it. I humbly lay bare my sincerest devotion, offering solemn gratitude to the Perfected. May the sacred person be safeguarded, and his celestial longevity further extended. May the imperial throne flourish, steadfast as bedrock. May winds be gentle and rains timely, yielding abundant harvests. May rivers run clear and seas remain calm, ushering in eternal peace and harmony. May sun and moon shine together, securing the imperial realm for ten thousand generations. May heaven and earth nurture all, gathering every blessing for the multitudes.

I pray that my singular devotion be beheld from above, and that supreme blessings be bestowed through the wondrous Dao. May all be attuned to harmony, and may this serve as testimony.

On the fifteenth day of the second month in the *jihai* year of the seventeenth year of *Yongle*, the altar was established; on the twenty-first day, the rites were concluded.

**Prayer of Dedication**
For the new and full moons of every month.

Prostrate in reverence, we turn our hearts to the Golden Gates, proclaiming the sacred scriptures from the jeweled caskets of the Perfected. Bowing at the jade steps, we pray for the sagely longevity of the imperial throne beneath the maple hall. Fragrant clouds swirl as we reverently kindle incense in the censer.

With utmost devotion, we make offerings to the Nine Heavens’ Golden Gates, Illuminated Dao and Penetrating Virtue, Great Immortal of Manifest Numinosity, Vast Salvation, Pure Subtlety, Cavernous Mystery, Tranquil Emptiness, Wondrous Response, Compassionate and Benevolent Protector of the Nation and Shelter of the People, Great Merciful Perfected Lord; and to the Nine Heavens’ Jade Gates, Proclaiming Transformation and Upholding the Teachings, Supreme Immortal of Radiant Numinosity, Vast Salvation, Lofty Clarity, Profound Stillness, Tranquil Purity, Wondrous Response, Benevolent and Kind Assistant of the Nation and Guardian of the People, Great Merciful Perfected Lord.

To the Sacred Father, Sacred Mother, Sacred Consort, Sacred Son, Sacred Grandson, the assembled majestic numina of the hall; to the Five Great Marshals—Zha, Bian, Wei, Zhao, and Diao—and the Two Marshals, Yue and Xu; to the attendant guardian immortals, the palace earth deities, and the Perfected Officials protecting the teachings: by this true incense, we universally offer homage to the Hong’en Lingji Palace.

On this morning of the new or full moon, we humbly gather the Daoist assembly and reverently proceed to the palace hall. We present incense, raise music, chant scriptures and invocations, perform the Daoist circumambulation, and dedicate the offerings. We earnestly beseech the Great Compassion to deign to perceive our sincerity.

May our prayers ascend through the Three Realms, reaching the Ninefold Heights. We reverently pray that the One Man be blessed, his longevity boundless. May his virtue renew daily, ever renewing. May he embody the enduring vastness of heaven and earth, his life spanning ten thousand years, ten thousand times ten thousand years, as steadfast and tranquil as mountains and rivers.

May the Four Seas be serene, the Eight Directions at peace. May the people dwell in safety, all things flourish, winds be gentle, and rains timely. With profound reverence, we bow in submission and pray: Long live the reigning emperor, ten thousand years, ten thousand years, ten thousand times ten thousand years.

---

**Daily Dawn Offering**
Prostrate in the dim light of dawn, we face the celestial thoroughfare, not far away; with purified hearts, we serve the Emperor, knocking at the Golden Gates, not distant. With the sincerity of humble grass, we look up to the lofty hearing of the exalted. Today, we burn incense and devoutly offer to the Nine Heavens’ Golden Gates and the Nine Heavens’ Jade Gates.

To the Sacred Father, Sacred Mother, Sacred Consort, Sacred Son, Sacred Grandson, the assembled numinous presences of the hall; to the Five Great Marshals—Zha, Bian, Wei, Zhao, and Diao—and the Two Marshals, Xu and Yue; to the attendant guardian immortals, the palace earth deities, and the Perfected Officials protecting the teachings: by this true incense, we universally offer homage to the Hong’en Lingji Palace.

This dawn, we humbly gather the Daoist assembly and reverently proceed to the palace hall. We present incense, offer praises, chant scriptures and invocations. We earnestly beseech the Great Compassion to deign to perceive our sincerity.

May our prayers ascend through the Three Realms, reaching the Ninefold Heights. We reverently pray that boundless mercy be universally bestowed, and sagely virtue shine resplendent. May the myriad nations under the Four Seas forever enjoy the governance of peace and prosperity. May the Five Winds and Ten Rains bring abundant harvests. May the sacred longevity be eternally secure, the imperial realm unshakable. May blessings extend to all beings, and fortune embrace the multitudes.

---

**Seasonal Observances**
Prostrate, we acknowledge the turning of the four seasons, nurturing transformation and growth through imperial virtue. The myriad regions, tranquil and harmonious, all rely on divine power. As auspicious festivals arrive, we humbly continue our meager offerings.

Today, we burn incense and devoutly offer to the Nine Heavens’ Golden Gates and the Nine Heavens’ Jade Gates. To the Sacred Father, Sacred Mother, Sacred Consort, Sacred Son, Sacred Grandson: by this true incense, we universally offer homage to the Hong’en Lingji Palace. As we encounter this propitious occasion, we prepare seasonal rites and humbly gather the Daoist assembly. We chant scriptures and invocations, dedicating the offerings.

We reverently pray that the true numina perceive our sincerity and bestow vast, salvific mercy. May beneficent blessings spread widely, bringing timely rains and sunshine. We pray for the imperial realm to be as steadfast as bedrock, and for the sacred longevity to equal the heavens. Extending to all living beings, may they equally partake in fortune and benefit. In celebration and praise, we bow.

On this Sacred Festival, your servant [Name], reverently upholding the imperial command and dutifully serving the numinous shrine, bears the transformative power of the Sagely August Rule and feels the sheltering virtue of the Perfected Lords. Unable to fully repay such grace, I turn in devotion and reverence. From the first peak of Mount Golden Ao, I gaze toward the nine-tiered jade steps of the imperial throne.

Reflecting upon this day, the [specific date] of the present month, I humbly recall: as the Purple Pivot records auspicious signs, this propitious occasion unfolds the flourishing era of celestial longevity. With a heart of sincerity, I offer the threefold felicitations of Hua’s borderlands. In advance of this day, I have respectfully assembled the Daoist clergy within this palace. For three days, we shall open the Daoist sanctuary, displaying the precious forms of all Perfected Ones. In solemn harmony, we prostrate with reverent sincerity; in radiant clarity, we seem to behold the dragon countenance near at hand. With praise and celebration, we extend longevity and blessings.

Today, I shall memorialize this to Heaven and Earth and submit petitions to the Perfected Offices. We shall establish a pure altar, conduct rites according to the sacred codes, and hold a grand purification offering for the Perfected Lords. We shall perform the Lamp Rite of Original Vows, reverently dedicating it to all deities. Further, we shall conduct jiao rites and perform secret scriptures. Upon the completion of these virtuous deeds, we shall hold a jiao offering to express gratitude.

Reverently praying for blessings and abundant fortune, we humbly beseech that His Imperial Majesty’s benevolence equal Heaven and Earth, his sagely years match the sun and moon in radiance. May his sacred longevity endure like mountains and rivers, as eternal as the cosmos. May auspicious signs repeatedly manifest, and the myriad treasures ever flourish. May the common folk joyfully sing while tilling the soil, and foreign lands hasten to present tribute. My heart brims with fervent devotion, awaiting the boundless grace to come.

With utmost reverence, I present this for the thousand autumns to come.

Your humble servant, holding office at the sacred shrine, has been graced by the radiance of the vermilion steps. My person ascends the turtle’s summit, where I gaze reverently toward the Azure Palace. On this propitious morning, as stars over the islets manifest their auspices, all within the realm prostrate themselves in joyful homage.

On this day of the present month, I devoutly gather the Daoist assembly to this very palace, where we follow the prescribed rites to inaugurate the Daoist arena. We proclaim our humble devotion and recite the profound scriptures. At dawn, we establish the Pure Offering to the True Lord, extol the Star Lamps of the Northern Dipper, and perform the secret scriptures. Upon the completion of these virtuous deeds, we hold a jiao offering to express gratitude.

Reverently praying for abundant blessings, we humbly beseech that His Highness the Crown Prince, inheriting the ancestral virtue, succeed to the eternal foundation. May he brilliantly assist the sagely model and enjoy a longevity of a thousand autumns. May he further strengthen the great root and personally embody utmost benevolence. May the Chinese and barbarians alike unite in harmony, and gods and men rejoice in his rule.

My heart brims with fervent devotion, awaiting the boundless grace to come. With utmost reverence, I present this.

On this auspicious dawn at the Golden Palace,

Your faithful servant, an official, prostrates himself. Since ancient times, the immortal’s name has been inscribed upon the lofty steps for his achievements in the Eastern Sea. His divine traces in the southern lands have manifested great blessings in this flourishing age. Loyal in upholding the altars of state, he is called upright and enlightened; benevolent toward all living beings, he brings them peace, ease, wealth, and longevity. Now, as auspicious omens descend from the Dipper’s abode, we specially offer praise and celebration in the Jade Palace.

With reverence, on the seventeenth day of the ninth month, we gather the Daoist assembly at this palace and follow the prescribed rites to inaugurate the Daoist arena. We convey our sincere devotion, kindle the Star Lamps, and extol the original vows. We specially establish the Pure Offering, transforming ordinary tributes into sacred rites. Invoking the True Compassion, we reverently pray for abundant fortune.

We humbly beseech that His Imperial Majesty’s longevity equal the mountains, his reign proclaimed to the four barbarians. May his virtue blanket Heaven and Earth, his dominion extend over ten thousand lands. May auspicious charts and propitious records flow unceasingly from the historians’ brushes. May surplus grain and lingering harvests repeatedly fulfill the farmers’ hopes. May court and countryside alike rejoice, and gods and men achieve harmony.

My heart brims with awe and devotion, awaiting the boundless grace to come. With utmost reverence, I present this.

On this auspicious dawn at the Jade Palace.

The faithful official [Name], with utmost reverence, makes a great vow within the Five Illuminations Palace, multiplying his form to uphold the Daoist teachings. At the Dragon’s Head of Three Mountains, he expounds the wondrous Dao, manifesting traces to achieve success. He illuminates divine beneficence to aid the myriad ages, assisting the state and protecting the people in this present day.

Reflecting with awe upon the imperial command, I reverently serve the numinous perfected. Moved by the sagely governance and transformative grace of the August Thearch, I bear the benevolent blessings of the transcendent immortals. With no means to repay such kindness, I turn my thoughts to cultivation and reverence. Now, on this propitious occasion of the Middle Prime Festival of the Earth Official, and the auspicious dawn of the August Graceful Perfected Lord, I humbly lay bare my sincerest devotion, offering it up to the exalted and luminous.

With deepest respect, I ascend the first Golden Roc, gazing reverently toward the Jade Palace of the Nine Heavens. I extend this celebration in humble gratitude, a small repayment for boundless favor. On this day, I devoutly gather the Daoist clergy, following the rituals to perform the rites. Spreading forth my sincere intent, I open the sacred precinct. I kindle and offer the Seven Luminaries’ star lamps, chanting the numinous scriptures of the original vows. Again, I establish the Pure Offering, presenting ordinary tributes as sacred rites. I manifest my thanks for Heaven’s grace, reverently praying for abundant fortune.

May the sagely longevity equal the enduring firmament, and the imperial enterprise be as steadfast as the mountains. May the Three Lights remain whole and the seasons harmonious, the Five Grains ripen and the people flourish. May the temple courtyards be solemn and serene, bringing peace and well-being to all beings. May the faithful who take refuge all rely upon the aid and protection of the cloud-like heavens.

My heart brims with awe and devotion, awaiting the boundless grace to come. With utmost reverence, I present this.

The Divine Consort of Jingguo on this Auspicious Dawn,

Your humble servant [Name], prostrate in reverence, gazes toward Ao Peak, honored by the sacred commendation of steadfast response. Adorned in ceremonial robes, she magnifies the virtue of bestowing life, in harmony above with the Golden Towers and below with the Petal Palaces.

Now, as the celestial pivot turns in its propitious cycle and this joyous birthday aligns with felicitous omens, I offer my exultant congratulations and humble gratitude for her august benevolence. With utmost devotion, on the thirteenth day of the first month, I gather the Daoist assembly to perform the rites in accordance with the sacred canons. I establish a grand Offering dedicated to the Divine Consort, chanting the numinous scriptures of the Petal Canon. Extending reverence to all the celestial palaces, I present these modest tributes, circling the ritual altar in hope of her boundless grace.

May the imperial enterprise stand firm, as unshakable as bedrock. May the imperial lineage flourish and prosper, extending its branches through ten thousand generations. May transformative governance bring moral beauty, and the people’s songs resound like the harmonious *fuyi*. May the qi flow in harmony with the seasons, and the land present auspicious omens of jade-like lingzhi. Overwhelmed with gratitude, I pray for eternal peace and prosperity.

My heart brims with awe and devotion beyond measure. With utmost reverence, I present this.

On the Auspicious Dawn of the Divine Consort of State-Protection,
this humble official [Name] prostrates himself, reflecting thus:

Her virtue is marked by grace, gentleness, reverence, and tranquility, perfectly harmonizing with the Jade Realm. Her pure and refined demeanor bestows life, and she has long been ranked among the celestial ranks. Flowing with elegance, she embodies serene majesty.

Now, on this propitious dawn of her birth, I humbly offer my modest sincerity in celebration. On the seventeenth day of the seventh month, I reverently gather the Daoist clergy to uphold the rites and perform a grand Offering dedicated to the Divine Consort, chanting the numinous scriptures of the Petal Canon. Extending reverence to all the celestial palaces, I present these modest tributes, circling the ritual altar in hope of her boundless grace.

May the imperial longevity endure, bestowing the celestial patterns for ten thousand years. May sagely governance bring harmony, uniting all under heaven in shared culture and virtue. May blessings extend to the imperial lineage, and her power embrace both spirits and mortals. May yin and yang harmonize like the balanced flame of the jade candle, and the elderly enjoy the joys of Huaxu.

My heart brims with awe and devotion beyond measure. With utmost reverence, I present this.

**Ritual Protocol for Sacrificial Offerings**
*Document No. 52, Verified by the Ministry of Rites at the Temporary Court*

1. **Sacrificial Offerings**: Two altars in total.
   - Each altar includes: one sheep and one pig, three kinds of fruit, one bolt of silk, and white ritual silk as prescribed by protocol.
   - The above offerings shall be procured with official funds, exempt from confiscation or penalty.

2. **Ritual Protocol**:
   - Six officiants shall be appointed.
   - The *Zanyin* (usher) shall guide the presenting official to the washing station, where the *Zan* (assistant) shall instruct the donning of the *zhi* (ritual tablet).
   - After washing, the *Zan* shall announce the departure.
   - The *Zanyin* shall lead the official to the position, whereupon music begins. The *Zan* shall instruct four bows, and the music ceases.
   - The *Zan* shall announce the presentation of silk, followed by the initial libation.
   - The substitute shall approach the divine position, and the *Zan* shall instruct the donning of the *zhi*.
   - The officiants shall present the silk to the presenting official, followed by the offering of the cup. The *zhi* shall then be removed.
   - The *Zan* shall instruct the substitute to proceed to the prayer-reading position and kneel. After the prayer is read, the *Zan* shall instruct prostration, rising, and standing.
   - The *Zan* shall announce the secondary libation, after which the officiants shall complete the offering.
   - The *Zan* shall instruct four bows, followed by the burning of the prayer and silk. The substitute shall proceed to the burning site, and the ritual shall conclude.

3. **Sacrificial Schedule**: Conducted biannually in spring and autumn, on a chosen day of the second month.

4. **Sacrificial Prayer**:
   In the year [Year], in the [Month] month, on the [Day] day of the lunar cycle, the Emperor dispatches [Name] to offer sacrifice to...

To the Radiant Perfected Lords of the Nine Heavens’ Golden Gates, who embody the Illuminated Dao and manifest virtue, the Great Immortals of boundless efficacy—those of the Pure Subtlety, Cavernous Mystery, and Empty Void—whose wondrous responsiveness, compassion, and grace shield the realm and shelter the people with vast benevolence:

To the Perfected Lords of the Nine Heavens’ Jade Gates, who proclaim transformation and uphold the teachings, the Exalted Immortals of far-reaching efficacy—those of lofty clarity, vast tranquility, and profound serenity—whose wondrous resonance, benevolence, and mercy assist the state and protect the people with boundless grace:

It is said:
These deities, entrusted with office in the Nine Heavens, manifest their numinous power in the southern lands. They spread their protection over the common folk, lend their wings to the state, and through the subtlety of the Dao and the profundity of virtue, their merits tower and their deeds shine forth. Thus, in accord with ritual propriety, they are honored with steadfast sacrifices each year. Now, at the mid-spring and mid-autumn seasons, we reverently present offerings of sacrificial animals and sweet wine. May they deign to partake.

Two altars are arranged.

For each altar:
Officials are appointed to conduct the rites.

On the fourth day of the eighth month in the seventh year of Yongle (1409), the imperial court appointed the officiating official Fang Wenzhao, who was charged solely with these duties and exempted from other administrative affairs. This Fang Wenzhao is the twelfth-generation descendant of Fang Jue, the benefactor of his ancestral temple. In the first year of Yongle (1403), he was initially summoned to the Ministry of Personnel as a tax-paying commoner of exceptional talent, where he served in probationary office before being granted his current position. He was selected to tend the Daoist incense.

On the eleventh day of the seventh month in the twelfth year of Yongle (1414), Minister of War Fang Bin and Commander of the Embroidered Uniform Guard Lin Guan received the imperial decree: "The Hong’en Lingji Palace in Fujian lacks Daoist priests to tend the incense and flame. Zhou, the Director of the Bureau of Rites, shall proceed there and instruct the local authorities to select twelve sincere and devout Daoists to serve in the palace, tending the incense and flame. Each shall be allotted five *dou* of grain and rice monthly." Respectfully received.

Ministry of Rites Document No. 76: After verification, the following were selected and dispatched to the palace:
Lin Shineng, Tu Zongju, Huang Zhikong, Jiang Ba, Hong Boda, Mao Haisheng, Chen Zhihu, Zeng Daosheng, Lin Zhifu, Zheng Wei, Wu Longxun, Liu Wenxu.

Assigned as households for sweeping and guarding:
Wan Yun, Lin Fa, Lin Dexian, Zhan Ying, Zheng Yong. The above five households were first assigned to sweeping duties.

Lin Zhen, Lin Shun, Lin Da, Lin Zheng, Lin Rong, Lin Fubao, Lin Shen, Sun Mei, Sun Zhulang, Ding Chendi, Jiang Meidi, Guo Dilang, Liu Yu, Chen Meidi, Zhao Yuan, Bian Yuan. The above sixteen households were subsequently added as guards.

Collectively, Ministry of Rites Autumn Document No. 335 verified and granted exemption from corvée for these households.

*Xu Xianzhen Lu*, Scroll Five: Temple Properties.

Hong’en Jizu Temple—Fields and Gardens.

**Fields:**
- Total: 6 *mu* 9 *fen*.
  - Summer tax: 29 *wen* in banknotes.
  - Autumn grain: 3 *dou* 9 *sheng* 1 *ge* (including both standard and supplementary levies).

  - Per *mu* assessment: 5 *sheng* 4 *ge* 2 standard grain.
  - Summer tax: 21 *wen* in banknotes.
  - Autumn grain: 2 *dou* 8 *sheng* 4 *ge* (including both standard and supplementary levies).
